So much of himself -- of his imagination and all other power -- have be lavish on the study of Walter and Elinor that he almost regard them a creation of his own , like the thousand with which he have people the realm of Picture .
Therefore do they flit through the twilight of the wood , hover on the mist of waterfall , look forth from the mirror of the lake , nor melt away in the noontide sun .
They haunt his pictorial fancy , not a mockery of life nor pale goblin of the dead , but in the guise of portrait , each with an unalterable expression which his magic have evoke from the cavern of the soul .
He could not recross the Atlantic till he have again behold the original of those airy picture .
`` O glorious Art ! ''
Thus muse the enthusiastic painter a he tread the street .
`` Thou art the image of the Creator 's own .
The innumerable form that wander in nothingness start into be at thy beck .
The dead live again ; thou recallest them to their old scene and givest their gray shadow the lustre of a good life , at once earthly and immortal .
Thou snatchest back the fleeting moment of history .
With then there be no past , for at thy touch all that be great becomes for ever present , and illustrious men live through long age in the visible performance of the very deeds which make them what they be .
O potent Art !
a thou bringest the faintly-revealed past to stand in that narrow strip of sunlight which we call ` now , ' canst thou summon the shrouded future to meet her there ?
Have I not achieve it ?
Am I not thy prophet ? ''
Thus with a proud yet melancholy fervor do he almost cry aloud a he pass through the toilsome street among people that know not of his revery nor could understand nor care for them .
It be not good for man to cherish a solitary ambition .
Unless there be those around him by whose example he may regulate himself , his thought , desire and hope will become extravagant and he the semblance -- perhaps the reality -- of a madman .
Reading other bosom with an acuteness almost preternatural , the painter fail to see the disorder of his own .
`` And this should be the house , '' say he , look up and down the front before he knock .
`` Heaven help my brain !
That picture !
Methinks it will never vanish .
Whether I look at the window or the door , there it be frame within them , paint strongly and glow in the rich tint -- the face of the portrait , the figure and action of the sketch ! ''
He knock .
`` The portrait -- be they within ? ''
inquire he of the domestic ; then , recollect himself , `` Your master and mistress -- be they at home ? ''
`` They be , sir , '' say the servant , add , a he notice that picturesque aspect of which the painter could never divest himself , `` and the portrait too . ''
The guest be admit into a parlor communicating by a central door with an interior room of the same size .
As the first apartment be empty , he pass to the entrance of the second , within which his eye be greet by those living personage , as well a their pictured representative , who have long be the object of so singular an interest .

They have not perceive his approach .

The picture , conceal for month , gleam forth again in undiminished splendor , appear to throw a sombre light across the room rather than to be disclose by a borrow radiance .
That of Elinor have be almost prophetic .

A mixture of affright would now have make it the very expression of the portrait .

The painter seem to hear the step of Destiny approach behind him on it progress toward it victim .
A strange thought dart into his mind .
Was not his own the form in which that Destiny have embody itself , and he a chief agent of the come evil which he have foreshadow ?
Still , Walter remain silent before the picture , commune with it a with his own heart and abandon himself to the spell of evil influence that the painter have cast upon the feature .
Gradually his eye kindle , while a Elinor watch the increase wildness of his face her own assume a look of terror ; and when , at last , he turn upon her , the resemblance of both to their portrait be complete .
`` Our fate be upon u ! ''
howl Walter .
`` Die ! ''

In the action and in the look and attitude of each the painter behold the figure of his sketch .
The picture , with all it tremendous coloring , be finish .
`` Hold , madman ! ''

He have advance from the door and interpose himself between the wretched being with the same sense of power to regulate their destiny a to alter a scene upon the canvas .
He stand like a magician control the phantom which he have evoke .
`` What ! ''
mutter Walter Ludlow a he relapse from fierce excitement into sullen gloom .
`` Does Fate impede it own decree ? ''
`` Wretched lady , '' say the painter , `` do I not warn you ? ''
`` You do , '' reply Elinor , calmly , a her terror give place to the quiet grief which it have disturb .
`` But I love him . ''
Is there not a deep moral in the tale ?
Could the result of one or all our deed be shadow forth and set before u , some would call it fate and hurry onward , others be sweep along by their passionate desire , and none be turn aside by the prophetic picture .
DAVID SWAN .
A FANTASY .
We can be but partially acquaint even with the event which actually influence our course through life and our final destiny .
There be innumerable other event , if such they may be call , which come close upon u , yet pass away without actual result or even betray their near approach by the reflection of any light or shadow across our mind .
Could we know all the vicissitude of our fortune , life would be too full of hope and fear , exultation or disappointment , to afford u a single hour of true serenity .
This idea may be illustrate by a page from the secret history of David Swan .
We have nothing to do with David until we find him , at the age of twenty , on the high road from his native place to the city of Boston , where his uncle , a small dealer in the grocery line , be to take him behind the counter .
Be it enough to say that he be a native of New Hampshire , born of respectable parent , and have receive an ordinary school education with a classic finish by a year at Gilmanton Academy .
After journey on foot from sunrise till nearly noon of a summer 's day , his weariness and the increase heat determine him to sit down in the first convenient shade and await the come up of the stage-coach .
As if plant on purpose for him , there soon appear a little tuft of maple with a delightful recess in the midst , and such a fresh bubbling spring that it seem never to have sparkle for any wayfarer but David Swan .
Virgin or not , he kiss it with his thirsty lip and then fling himself along the brink , pillow his head upon some shirt and a pair of pantaloon tie up in a striped cotton handkerchief .
The sunbeam could not reach him ; the dust do not yet rise from the road after the heavy rain of yesterday , and his grassy lair suit the young man well than a bed of down .
The spring murmur drowsily beside him ; the branch wave dreamily across the blue sky overhead , and a deep sleep , perchance hiding dream within it depth , fell upon David Swan .
But we be to relate event which he do not dream of .
While he lay sound asleep in the shade other people be wide awake , and pass to and fro , afoot , on horseback and in all sort of vehicle , along the sunny road by his bedchamber .
Some look neither to the right hand nor the left and know not that he be there ; some merely glance that way without admit the slumberer among their busy thought ; some laugh to see how soundly he sleep , and several whose heart be brim full of scorn eject their venomous superfluity on David Swan .
A middle-aged widow , when nobody else be near , thrust her head a little way into the recess , and vow that the young fellow look charm in his sleep .
A temperance lecturer saw him , and work poor David into the texture of his evening 's discourse a an awful instance of dead drunkenness by the roadside .
But censure , praise , merriment , scorn and indifference be all one -- or , rather , all nothing -- to David Swan .
He have sleep only a few moment when a brown carriage draw by a handsome pair of horse bowl easily along and be bring to a standstill nearly in front of David 's resting-place .
A linch-pin have fall out and permit one of the wheel to slide off .
The damage be slight and occasion merely a momentary alarm to an elderly merchant and his wife , who be return to Boston in the carriage .
While the coachman and a servant be replace the wheel the lady and gentleman shelter themselves beneath the maple tree , and there espy the bubbling fountain and David Swan asleep beside it .
Impressed with the awe which the humble sleeper usually shed around him , the merchant trod as lightly a the gout would allow , and his spouse take good heed not to rustle her silk gown l David should start up all of a sudden .
`` How soundly he sleep ! ''
whisper the old gentleman .
`` From what a depth he draw that easy breath !
Such sleep a that , bring on without an opiate , would be worth more to me than half my income , for it would suppose health and an untroubled mind . ''
`` And youth besides , '' say the lady .
`` Healthy and quiet age do not sleep thus .
Our slumber be no more like his than our wakefulness . ''
The longer they look , the more do this elderly couple feel interested in the unknown youth to whom the wayside and the maple shade be a a secret chamber with the rich gloom of damask curtain brood over him .
Perceiving that a stray sunbeam glimmer down upon his face , the lady contrive to twist a branch aside so a to intercept it , and , have do this little act of kindness , she begin to feel like a mother to him .
`` Providence seem to have lay him here , '' whisper she to her husband , `` and to have bring u hither to find him , after our disappointment in our cousin 's son .
Methinks I can see a likeness to our departed Henry .
Shall we waken him ? ''
`` To what purpose ? ''
say the merchant , hesitate .
`` We know nothing of the youth 's character . ''
`` That open countenance ! ''
reply his wife , in the same hushed voice , yet earnestly .
`` This innocent sleep ! ''
While these whisper be pass , the sleeper 's heart do not throb , nor his breath become agitate , nor his feature betray the least token of interest .
Yet Fortune be bend over him , just ready to let fall a burden of gold .
The old merchant have lose his only son , and have no heir to his wealth except a distant relative with whose conduct he be dissatisfy .
In such case people sometimes do strange thing than to act the magician and awaken a young man to splendor who fell asleep in poverty .
`` Shall we not waken him ? ''
repeat the lady , persuasively .
`` The coach be ready , sir , '' say the servant , behind .
The old couple start , redden and hurry away , mutually wonder that they should ever have dream of do anything so very ridiculous .
The merchant throw himself back in the carriage and occupy his mind with the plan of a magnificent asylum for unfortunate men of business .
Meanwhile , David Swan enjoy his nap .
The carriage could not have go above a mile or two when a pretty young girl come along with a trip pace which show precisely how her little heart be dance in her bosom .
Perhaps it be this merry kind of motion that cause -- be there any harm in say it ?
-- her garter to slip it knot .
Conscious that the silken girth -- if silk it be -- be relax it hold , she turn aside into the shelter of the maple tree , and there find a young man asleep by the spring .

But there be peril near the sleeper .
A monster of a bee have be wander overhead -- buzz , buzz , buzz -- now among the leaf , now flash through the strip of sunshine , and now lose in the dark shade , till finally he appear to be settle on the eyelid of David Swan .
The sting of a bee be sometimes deadly .

How sweet a picture !
This good deed accomplish , with quicken breath and a deep blush she steal a glance at the youthful stranger for whom she have be battle with a dragon in the air .
`` He be handsome ! ''
thought she , and blush redder yet .
How could it be that no dream of bliss grow so strong within him that , shatter by it very strength , it should part asunder and allow him to perceive the girl among it phantom ?
Why , at least , do no smile of welcome brighten upon his face ?
She be come , the maid whose soul , accord to the old and beautiful idea , have be sever from his own , and whom in all his vague but passionate desire he yearn to meet .
Her only could he love with a perfect love , him only could she receive into the depth of her heart , and now her image be faintly blush in the fountain by his side ; should it pass away , it happy lustre would never gleam upon his life again .

She depart , but do not trip along the road so lightly a when she come .
Now , this girl 's father be a thriving country merchant in the neighborhood , and happen at that identical time to be look out for just such a young man a David Swan .
Had David form a wayside acquaintance with the daughter , he would have become the father 's clerk , and all else in natural succession .
So here , again , have good fortune -- the best of fortune -- steal so near that her garment brush against him , and he know nothing of the matter .
The girl be hardly out of sight when two men turn aside beneath the maple shade .
Both have dark face set off by cloth cap , which be draw down aslant over their brow .
Their dress be shabby , yet have a certain smartness .

Do you see that bundle under his head ? ''
The other villain nod , wink and leer .
`` I 'll bet you a horn of brandy , '' say the first , `` that the chap have either a pocketbook or a snug little hoard of small change stow away amongst his shirt .
And if not there , we will find it in his pantaloon pocket . ''
`` But how if he wake ? ''
say the other .
His companion thrust aside his waistcoat , point to the handle of a dirk and nod .
`` So be it ! ''
mutter the second villain .
They approach the unconscious David , and , while one point the dagger toward his heart , the other begin to search the bundle beneath his head .
Their two face , grim , wrinkle and ghastly with guilt and fear , bent over their victim , look horrible enough to be mistake for fiend should he suddenly awake .
Nay , have the villain glance aside into the spring , even they would hardly have know themselves a reflect there .
But David Swan have never wear a more tranquil aspect , even when asleep on his mother 's breast .

`` If he stir , I 'll strike , '' mutter the other .
But at this moment a dog scent along the ground come in beneath the maple tree and gaze alternately at each of these wicked men and then at the quiet sleeper .
He then lap out of the fountain .
`` Pshaw ! ''
say one villain .
`` We can do nothing now .
The dog 's master must be close behind . ''
`` Let 's take a drink and be off , '' say the other .
The man with the dagger thrust back the weapon into his bosom and draw forth a pocket-pistol , but not of that kind which kill by a single discharge .
It be a flask of liquor with a block-tin tumbler screw upon the mouth .
Each drank a comfortable dram , and leave the spot with so many jest and such laughter at their unaccomplished wickedness that they might be say to have go on their way rejoicing .
In a few hour they have forget the whole affair , nor once imagine that the recording angel have write down the crime of murder against their soul in letter as durable a eternity .
As for David Swan , he still sleep quietly , neither conscious of the shadow of death when it hang over him nor of the glow of renew life when that shadow be withdraw .
He sleep , but no longer so quietly a at first .
An hour 's repose have snatch from his elastic frame the weariness with which many hour of toil have burden it .
Now he stir , now move his lip without a sound , now talk in an inward tone to the noonday spectre of his dream .
But a noise of wheel come rattle louder and louder along the road , until it dash through the dispersing mist of David 's slumber ; and there be the stagecoach .
He start up with all his idea about him .
`` Halloo , driver !
Take a passenger ? ''
shout he .
`` Room on top ! ''
answer the driver .
Up mount David , and bowl away merrily toward Boston without so much a a parting glance at that fountain of dreamlike vicissitude .
He know not that a phantom of Wealth have throw a golden hue upon it water , nor that one of Love have sigh softly to their murmur , nor that one of Death have threaten to crimson them with his blood , all in the brief hour since he lay down to sleep .
Sleeping or wake , we hear not the airy footstep of the strange thing that almost happen .
Does it not argue a superintending Providence that , while viewless and unexpected event thrust themselves continually athwart our path , there should still be regularity enough in mortal life to render foresight even partially available ?
SIGHTS FROM A STEEPLE .
So !
I have climb high , and my reward be small .
Here I stand with wearied knee -- earth , indeed , at a dizzy depth below , but heaven far , far beyond me still .
Oh that I could soar up into the very zenith , where man never breathe nor eagle ever fly , and where the ethereal azure melt away from the eye and appear only a deepened shade of nothingness !
And yet I shiver at that cold and solitary thought .
What cloud be gather in the golden west with direful intent against the brightness and the warmth of this summer afternoon ?
They be ponderous air-ships , black a death and freight with the tempest , and at interval their thunder -- the signal-guns of that unearthly squadron -- roll distant along the deep of heaven .
These near heap of fleecy vapor -- methinks I could roll and toss upon them the whole day long -- seem scatter here and there for the repose of tired pilgrim through the sky .
Perhaps -- for who can tell ?
-- beautiful spirit be disport themselves there , and will bless my mortal eye with the brief appearance of their curly lock of golden light and laugh face fair and faint a the people of a rosy dream .
Or where the float mass so imperfectly obstruct the color of the firmament a slender foot and fairy limb rest too heavily upon the frail support may be thrust through and suddenly withdrawn , while long fancy follow them in vain .
Yonder , again , be an airy archipelago where the sunbeam love to linger in their journeying through space .
Every one of those little cloud have be dip and steep in radiance which the slight pressure might disengage in silvery profusion like water wrung from a sea-maid 's hair .
Bright they be a a young man 's vision , and , like them , would be realize in dullness , obscurity and tear .
I will look on them no more .
In three part of the visible circle whose centre be this spire I discern cultivate field , village , white country-seats , the wave line of rivulet , little placid lake , and here and there a rise ground that would fain be term a hill .
On the fourth side be the sea , stretch away toward a viewless boundary , blue and calm except where the passing anger of a shadow flit across it surface and be go .
Hitherward a broad inlet penetrate far into the land ; on the verge of the harbor form by it extremity be a town , and over it be I , a watchman , all-heeding and unheeded .
Oh that the multitude of chimney could speak , like those of Madrid , and betray in smoky whisper the secret of all who since their first foundation have assemble at the hearth within !
Oh that the Limping Devil of Le Sage would perch beside me here , extend his wand over this contiguity of roof , uncover every chamber and make me familiar with their inhabitant !
The most desirable mode of existence might be that of a spiritualized Paul Pry hover invisible round man and woman , witness their deed , search into their heart , borrow brightness from their felicity and shade from their sorrow , and retain no emotion peculiar to himself .
But none of these thing be possible ; and if I would know the interior of brick wall or the mystery of human bosom , I can but guess .
Yonder be a fair street extend north and south .
The stately mansion be place each on it carpet of verdant grass , and a long flight of step descends from every door to the pavement .
Ornamental tree -- the broadleafed horse-chestnut , the elm so lofty and bending , the graceful but infrequent willow , and others whereof I know not the name -- grow thrivingly among brick and stone .
The oblique ray of the sun be intercept by these green citizen and by the house , so that one side of the street be a shaded and pleasant walk .
On it whole extent there be now but a single passenger , advance from the upper end , and he , unless distance and the medium of a pocket spyglass do him more than justice , be a fine young man of twenty .
He saunter slowly forward , slap his left hand with his folded glove , bend his eye upon the pavement , and sometimes raise them to throw a glance before him .
Certainly he have a pensive air .
Is he in doubt or in debt ?
Is he -- if the question be allowable -- in love ?
Does he strive to be melancholy and gentlemanlike , or be he merely overcome by the heat ?
But I bid him farewell for the present .
The door of one of the house -- an aristocratic edifice with curtain of purple and gold waving from the window -- be now open , and down the step come two lady swing their parasol and lightly array for a summer ramble .
Both be young , both be pretty ; but methinks the left-hand lass be the fairer of the twain , and , though she be so serious at this moment , I could swear that there be a treasure of gentle fun within her .
They stand talk a little while upon the step , and finally proceed up the street .
Meantime , a their face be now turn from me , I may look elsewhere .
Upon that wharf and down the corresponding street be a busy contrast to the quiet scene which I have just notice .
Business evidently have it centre there , and many a man be waste the summer afternoon in labor and anxiety , in lose rich or in gain them , when he would be wise to flee away to some pleasant country village or shade lake in the forest or wild and cool sea-beach .
I see vessels unlade at the wharf and precious merchandise strown upon the ground abundantly a at the bottom of the sea -- that market whence no good return , and where there be no captain nor supercargo to render an account of sale .
Here the clerk be diligent with their paper and pencil and sailor ply the block and tackle that hang over the hold , accompany their toil with cry long-drawn and roughly melodious till the bale and puncheons ascend to upper air .
At a little distance a group of gentleman be assemble round the door of a warehouse .
Grave senior be they , and I would wager -- if it be safe , in these time , to be responsible for any one -- that the least eminent among them might vie with old Vincentio , that incomparable trafficker of Pisa .
I can even select the wealthy of the company .
It be the elderly personage in somewhat rusty black , with powdered hair the superfluous whiteness of which be visible upon the cape of his coat .
His twenty ship be waft on some of their many course by every breeze that blow , and his name , I will venture to say , though I know it not , be a familiar sound among the far-separated merchant of Europe and the Indies .
But I bestow too much of my attention in this quarter .
On look again to the long and shady walk I perceive that the two fair girl have encounter the young man .
After a sort of shyness in the recognition , he turn back with them .
Moreover , he have sanction my taste in regard to his companion by place himself on the inner side of the pavement , nearest the Venus to whom I , enact on a steeple-top the part of Paris on the top of Ida , adjudge the golden apple .
In two street converge at right angle toward my watch-tower I distinguish three different procession .
One be a proud array of voluntary soldier in bright uniform , resemble , from the height whence I look down , the painted veteran that garrison the window of a toy-shop .
And yet it stir my heart .
Their regular advance , their nodding plume , the sun-flash on their bayonet and musket-barrels , the roll of their drum ascend past me , and the fife ever and anon piercing through , -- these thing have waken a warlike fire , peaceful though I be .
Close to their rear march a battalion of schoolboy range in crooked and irregular platoon , shoulder stick , thump a harsh and unripe clatter from an instrument of tin and ridiculously ape the intricate manoeuvre of the foremost band .
Nevertheless , a slight difference be scarcely perceptible from a church-spire , one might be tempt to ask , `` Which be the boy ? ''
or , rather , `` Which the men ? ''
But , leave these , let u turn to the third procession , which , though sadder in outward show , may excite identical reflection in the thoughtful mind .
It be a funeral -- a hearse drawn by a black and bony steed and cover by a dusty pall , two or three coach rumble over the stone , their driver half asleep , a dozen couple of careless mourner in their every-day attire .
Such be not the fashion of our father when they carry a friend to his grave .
There be now no doleful clang of the bell to proclaim sorrow to the town .
Was the King of Terrors more awful in those day than in our own , that wisdom and philosophy have be able to produce this change ?
Not so .
Here be a proof that he retain his proper majesty .
The military men and the military boy be wheel round the corner , and meet the funeral full in the face .
Immediately the drum be silent , all but the tap that regulate each simultaneous footfall .
The soldier yield the path to the dusty hearse and unpretending train , and the child quit their rank and cluster on the sidewalk with timorous and instinctive curiosity .
The mourner enter the churchyard at the base of the steeple and pause by an open grave among the burial-stones ; the lightning glimmer on them a they lower down the coffin , and the thunder rattle heavily while they throw the earth upon it lid .
Verily , the shower be near , and I tremble for the young man and the girl , who have now disappear from the long and shady street .
How various be the situation of the people cover by the roof beneath me , and how diversified be the event at this moment befall them !
The new-born , the age , the dying , the strong in life and the recent dead be in the chamber of these many mansion .
The full of hope , the happy , the miserable and the desperate dwell together within the circle of my glance .
In some of the house over which my eye roam so coldly guilt be enter into heart that be still tenant by a debased and trodden virtue ; guilt be on the very edge of commission , and the impend deed might be avert ; guilt be do , and the criminal wonder if it be irrevocable .

Lo !
the raindrop be descend .
The cloud within a little time have gather over all the sky , hang heavily , a if about to drop in one unbroken mass upon the earth .
At interval the lightning flash from their brooding heart , quiver , disappears , and then come the thunder , travel slowly after it twin-born flame .
A strong wind have spring up , howl through the darkened street , and raise the dust in dense body to rebel against the approach storm .
