How often must his heart have be gladden by the delight of child a they view these animated figure , or his pride indulge by harangue learnedly to grow men on the mechanical power which produce such wonderful effect , or his gallantry bring into play -- for this be an attribute which such grave men do not lack -- by the visit of pretty maiden !
And then with how fresh a feeling must he return at interval to his own peculiar home !
`` I would I be assure of a happy a life a his , '' think I . Though the showman 's wagon might have accommodate fifteen or twenty spectator , it now contain only himself and me and a third person , at whom I throw a glance on entering .
He be a neat and trim young man of two or three and twenty ; his drab hat and green frock-coat with velvet collar be smart , though no long new , while a pair of green spectacle that seem needless to his brisk little eye give him something of a scholar-like and literary air .
After allow me a sufficient time to inspect the puppet , he advance with a bow and draw my attention to some book in a corner of the wagon .
These he forthwith begin to extol with an amazing volubility of well-sounding word and an ingenuity of praise that win him my heart a be myself one of the most merciful of critic .
Indeed , his stock require some considerable power of commendation in the salesman .
There be several ancient friend of mine -- the novel of those happy day when my affection waver between the Scottish Chiefs and Thomas Thumb -- besides a few of late date whose merit have not be acknowledge by the public .
I be glad to find that dear little venerable volume the New England Primer , look as antique a ever , though in it thousandth new edition ; a bundle of superannuated gilt picture-books make such a child of me that , partly for the glittering cover and partly for the fairy-tales within , I buy the whole , and an assortment of ballad and popular theatrical song draw largely on my purse .
To balance these expenditure , I meddle neither with sermon nor science nor morality , though volume of each be there , nor with a Life of Franklin in the coarsest of paper , but so showily bound that it be emblematical of the doctor himself in the court-dress which he refuse to wear at Paris , nor with Webster 's spelling-book , nor some of Byron 's minor poem , nor half a dozen little Testaments at twenty-five cent each .
Thus far the collection might have be sweep from some great bookstore or pick up at an even auction-room , but there be one small blue-covered pamphlet which the pedler hand me with so peculiar an air that I purchase it immediately at his own price ; and then for the first time the thought struck me that I have speak face to face with the veritable author of a printed book .
The literary-man now evince a great kindness for me , and I venture to inquire which way he be travel .

THE WHITE OLD MAID .
The moonbeam come through two deep and narrow window and show a spacious chamber richly furnish in an antique fashion .
From one lattice the shadow of the diamond pane be throw upon the floor ; the ghostly light through the other slept upon a bed , fall between the heavy silken curtain and illuminate the face of a young man .
But how quietly the slumberer lay !
how pale his feature !
And how like a shroud the sheet be wind about his frame !
Yes , it be a corpse in it burial-clothes .
Suddenly the fixed feature seem to move with dark emotion .
Strange fantasy !
It be but the shadow of the fringed curtain wave betwixt the dead face and the moonlight a the door of the chamber open and a girl stole softly to the bedside .
Was there delusion in the moonbeam , or do her gesture and her eye betray a gleam of triumph a she bend over the pale corpse , pale a itself , and press her living lip to the cold one of the dead ?
As she draw back from that long kiss her feature writhe a if a proud heart be fight with it anguish .
Again it seem that the feature of the corpse have move responsive to her own .
Still an illusion .
The silken curtain have wave a second time betwixt the dead face and the moonlight a another fair young girl unclosed the door and glide ghostlike to the bedside .
There the two maiden stand , both beautiful , with the pale beauty of the dead between them .
But she who have first enter be proud and stately , and the other a soft and fragile thing .
`` Away ! ''
cry the lofty one .
`` Thou hadst him live ; the dead be mine . ''
`` Thine ! ''
return the other , shudder .
`` Well hast thou speak ; the dead be thine . ''
The proud girl start and star into her face with a ghastly look , but a wild-and mournful expression pass across the feature of the gentle one , and , weak and helpless , she sink down on the bed , her head pillow beside that of the corpse and her hair mingle with his dark lock .
A creature of hope and joy , the first draught of sorrow have bewilder her .
`` Edith ! ''
cry her rival .
Edith groan a with a sudden compression of the heart , and , remove her cheek from the dead youth 's pillow , she stand upright , fearfully encounter the eye of the lofty girl .
`` Wilt thou betray me ? ''
say the latter , calmly .
`` Till the dead bid me speak I will be silent , '' answer Edith .
`` Leave u alone together .
Go and live many year , and then return and tell me of thy life .
He too will be here .
Then , if thou tellest of suffering more than death , we will both forgive thee . ''
`` And what shall be the token ? ''
ask the proud girl , a if her heart acknowledge a meaning in these wild word .
`` This lock of hair , '' say Edith , lift one of the dark cluster curl that lay heavily on the dead man 's brow .
The two maiden join their hand over the bosom of the corpse and appoint a day and hour far , far in time to come for their next meeting in that chamber .
The stately girl give one deep look at the motionless countenance and depart , yet turn again and tremble ere she close the door , almost believe that her dead lover frown upon her .
And Edith , too !
Was not her white form fading into the moonlight ?
Scorning her own weakness , she go forth and perceive that a negro slave be wait in the passage with a waxlight , which he hold between her face and his own and regard her , a she think , with an ugly expression of merriment .
Lifting his torch on high , the slave light her down the staircase and undo the portal of the mansion .
The young clergyman of the town have just ascend the step , and , bow to the lady , pass in without a word .
Years -- many year -- roll on .
The world seem new again , so much old be it grown since the night when those pale girl have clasp their hand across the bosom of the corpse .
In the interval a lonely woman have pass from youth to extreme age , and be know by all the town a the `` Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet . ''
A taint of insanity have affect her whole life , but so quiet , sad and gentle , so utterly free from violence , that she be suffer to pursue her harmless fantasy unmolested by the world with whose business or pleasures she have naught to do .
She dwell alone , and never come into the daylight except to follow funeral .
Whenever a corpse be bear along the street , in sunshine , rain or snow , whether a pompous train of the rich and proud thronged after it or few and humble be the mourner , behind them come the lonely woman in a long white garment which the people call her shroud .
She take no place among the kindred or the friend , but stand at the door to hear the funeral prayer , and walk in the rear of the procession a one whose earthly charge it be to haunt the house of mourning and be the shadow of affliction and see that the dead be duly bury .
So long have this be her custom that the inhabitant of the town deem her a part of every funeral , as much a the coffin-pall or the very corpse itself , and augur ill of the sinner 's destiny unless the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet come glide like a ghost behind .
Once , it be say , she affright a bridal-party with her pale presence , appear suddenly in the illuminated hall just a the priest be unite a false maid to a wealthy man before her lover have be dead a year .
Evil be the omen to that marriage .
Sometimes she stole forth by moonlight and visit the graf of venerable integrity and wed love and virgin innocence , and every spot where the ash of a kind and faithful heart be moulder .
Over the hillock of those favor dead would she stretch out her arm with a gesture a if she be scatter seed , and many believe that she bring them from the garden of Paradise , for the graf which she have visit be green beneath the snow and cover with sweet flower from April to November .
Her blessing be good than a holy verse upon the tombstone .
Thus wore away her long , sad , peaceful and fantastic life till few be so old a she , and the people of late generation wonder how the dead have ever be bury or mourner have endure their grief without the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet .
Still year go on , and still she follow funeral and be not yet summon to her own festival of death .
One afternoon the great street of the town be all alive with business and bustle , though the sun now gild only the upper half of the church-spire , have leave the housetop and lofty tree in shadow .
The scene be cheerful and animate in spite of the sombre shade between the high brick building .
Here be pompous merchant in white wig and lace velvet , the bronzed face of sea-captains , the foreign garb and air of Spanish Creoles , and the disdainful port of native of Old England , all contrast with the rough aspect of one or two back-settlers negotiate sale of timber from forest where axe have never sound .
Sometimes a lady pass , swell roundly forth in an embroidered petticoat , balance her step in high-heeled shoe and courtesying with lofty grace to the punctilious obeisance of the gentleman .
The life of the town seem to have it very centre not far from an old mansion that stand somewhat back from the pavement , surround by neglected grass , with a strange air of loneliness rather deepen than dispel by the throng so near it .
Its site would have be suitably occupy by a magnificent Exchange or a brick block letter all over with various sign , or the large house itself might have make a noble tavern with the `` King 's Arms '' swing before it and guest in every chamber , instead of the present solitude .
But , owe to some dispute about the right of inheritance , the mansion have be long without a tenant , decay from year to year and throw the stately gloom of it shadow over the busy part of the town .
Such be the scene , and such the time , when a figure unlike any that have be describe be observe at a distance down the street .
`` I espy a strange sail yonder , '' remark a Liverpool captain -- `` that woman in the long white garment . ''
The sailor seem much strike by the object , a be several others who at the same moment catch a glimpse of the figure that have attract his notice .
Almost immediately the various topic of conversation give place to speculation in an undertone on this unwonted occurrence .
`` Can there be a funeral so late this afternoon ? ''
inquire some .
They look for the sign of death at every door -- the sexton , the hearse , the assemblage of black-clad relative , all that make up the woeful pomp of funeral .
They raise their eye , also , to the sun-gilt spire of the church , and wonder that no clang proceed from it bell , which have always toll till now when this figure appear in the light of day .
But none have hear that a corpse be to be borne to it home that afternoon , nor be there any token of a funeral except the apparition of the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet .
`` What may this portend ? ''
ask each man of his neighbor .
All smile a they put the question , yet with a certain trouble in their eye , a if pestilence , or some other wide calamity , be prognosticate by the untimely intrusion among the living of one whose presence have always be associate with death and woe .
What a comet be to the earth be that sad woman to the town .
Still she move on , while the hum of surprise be hush at her approach , and the proud and the humble stood aside that her white garment might not wave against them .
It be a long , loose robe of spotless purity .
Its wearer appear very old , pale , emaciated and feeble , yet glide onward without the unsteady pace of extreme age .
At one point of her course a little rosy boy burst forth from a door and ran with open arm toward the ghostly woman , seem to expect a kiss from her bloodless lip .
She make a slight pause , fix her eye upon him with an expression of no earthly sweetness , so that the child shiver and stand awestruck rather than affright while the Old Maid pass on .
Perhaps her garment might have be pollute even by an infant 's touch ; perhaps her kiss would have be death to the sweet boy within the year .
`` She be but a shadow , '' whisper the superstitious .
`` The child put forth his arm and could not grasp her robe . ''
The wonder be increase when the Old Maid pass beneath the porch of the deserted mansion , ascend the moss-covered step , lift the iron knocker and give three rap .
The people could only conjecture that some old remembrance , trouble her bewildered brain , have impel the poor woman hither to visit the friend of her youth -- all go from their home long since and for ever unless their ghost still haunt it , fit company for the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet .
An elderly man approach the step , and , reverently uncover his gray lock , essay to explain the matter .
`` None , madam , '' say he , `` have dwell in this house these fifteen year agone -- no , not since the death of old Colonel Fenwicke , whose funeral you may remember to have follow .
His heir , be ill-agreed among themselves , have let the mansion-house go to ruin . ''
The Old Maid look slowly round with a slight gesture of one hand and a finger of the other upon her lip , appear more shadow-like than ever in the obscurity of the porch .
But again she lift the hammer , and give , this time , a single rap .
Could it be that a footstep be now heard come down the staircase of the old mansion which all conceive to have be so long untenanted ?
Slowly , feebly , yet heavily , like the pace of an age and infirm person , the step approach , more distinct on every downward stair , till it reach the portal .
The bar fell on the inside ; the door be open .

`` Who undo the door ? ''
ask many .
This question , owe to the depth of shadow beneath the porch , no one could satisfactorily answer .
Two or three age men , while protest against an inference which might be draw , affirm that the person within be a negro and bore a singular resemblance to old Csar , formerly a slave in the house , but free by death some thirty year before .
`` Her summons have wake up a servant of the old family , '' say one , half seriously .
`` Let u wait here , '' reply another ; `` more guest will knock at the door anon .
But the gate of the graveyard should be throw open . ''
Twilight have overspread the town before the crowd begin to separate or the comment on this incident be exhaust .
One after another be wend his way homeward , when a coach -- no common spectacle in those day -- drive slowly into the street .
It be an old-fashioned equipage , hang close to the ground , with arm on the panel , a footman behind and a grave , corpulent coachman seat high in front , the whole give an idea of solemn state and dignity .
There be something awful in the heavy rumbling of the wheel .
The coach roll down the street , till , come to the gateway of the deserted mansion , it draw up , and the footman sprang to the ground .
`` Whose grand coach be this ? ''
ask a very inquisitive body .
The footman make no reply , but ascend the step of the old house , give three tap with the iron hammer , and return to open the coach door .
An old man possess of the heraldic lore so common in that day examine the shield of arm on the panel .
`` Azure , a lion 's head erase , between three flower de luce , '' say he , then whisper the name of the family to whom these bearing belong .
The last inheritor of it honor be recently dead , after a long residence amid the splendor of the British court , where his birth and wealth have give him no mean station .
`` He leave no child , '' continue the herald , `` and these arm , be in a lozenge , betoken that the coach appertain to his widow . ''
Further disclosure , perhaps , might have be make have not the speaker be suddenly strike dumb by the stern eye of an ancient lady who thrust forth her head from the coach , prepare to descend .
As she emerge the people saw that her dress be magnificent , and her figure dignify in spite of age and infirmity -- a stately ruin , but with a look at once of pride and wretchedness .
Her strong and rigid feature have an awe about them unlike that of the white Old Maid , but a of something evil .
She pass up the step , lean on a gold-headed cane .
The door swung open a she ascend , and the light of a torch glitter on the embroidery of her dress and gleam on the pillar of the porch .
After a momentary pause , a glance backward and then a desperate effort , she go in .
The decipherer of the coat-of-arms have venture up the low step , and , shrink back immediately , pale and tremulous , affirm that the torch be hold by the very image of old Csar .
`` But such a hideous grin , '' add he , `` be never see on the face of mortal man , black or white .
It will haunt me till my dying-day . ''
Meantime , the coach have wheel round with a prodigious clatter on the pavement and rumble up the street , disappear in the twilight , while the ear still track it course .
Scarcely be it go when the people begin to question whether the coach and attendant , the ancient lady , the spectre of old Csar and the Old Maid herself be not all a strangely-combined delusion with some dark purport in it mystery .
The whole town be astir , so that , instead of dispersing , the crowd continually increase , and stand gaze up at the window of the mansion , now silver by the brightening moon .
The elder , glad to indulge the narrative propensity of age , tell of the long-faded splendor of the family , the entertainment they have give and the guest , the great of the land , and even title and noble one from abroad , who have pass beneath that portal .
These graphic reminiscence seem to call up the ghost of those to whom they refer .
So strong be the impression on some of the more imaginative hearer that two or three be seize with tremble fit at one and the same moment , protest that they have distinctly hear three other rap of the iron knocker .
`` Impossible ! ''
exclaim others .
`` See !
The moon shine beneath the porch , and show every part of it except in the narrow shade of that pillar .
There be no one there . ''
`` Did not the door open ? ''
whisper one of these fanciful person .
`` Didst thou see it too ? ''
say his companion , in a startled tone .
But the general sentiment be oppose to the idea that a third visitant have make application at the door of the deserted house .
A few , however , adhere to this new marvel , and even declare that a red gleam like that of a torch have shine through the great front window , a if the negro be light a guest up the staircase .
This too be pronounce a mere fantasy .
But at once the whole multitude start , and each man behold his own terror paint in the face of all the rest .
`` What an awful thing be this ! ''
cry they .
A shriek too fearfully distinct for doubt have be hear within the mansion , break forth suddenly and succeed by a deep stillness , a if a heart have burst in give it utterance .
The people know not whether to fly from the very sight of the house or to rush tremble in and search out the strange mystery .
Amid their confusion and affright they be somewhat reassure by the appearance of their clergyman , a venerable patriarch , and equally a saint , who have teach them and their father the way to heaven for more than the space of an ordinary lifetime .
He be a reverend figure with long white hair upon his shoulder , a white beard upon his breast and a back so bent over his staff that he seem to be look downward continually , a if to choose a proper grave for his weary frame .

`` Verily , '' say the old gentleman , `` it will be fit that I enter the mansion-house of the worthy Colonel Fenwicke , l any harm should have befall that true Christian woman whom ye call the ` Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet . ' ''
Behold , then , the venerable clergyman ascend the step of the mansion with a torch-bearer behind him .
It be the elderly man who have speak to the Old Maid , and the same who have afterward explain the shield of arm and recognize the feature of the negro .
Like their predecessor , they give three rap with the iron hammer .
`` Old Csar cometh not , '' observe the priest .
`` Well , I wot he no longer doth service in this mansion . ''
`` Assuredly , then , it be something worse in old Csar 's likeness , '' say the other adventurer .
`` Be it a God will , '' answer the clergyman .
`` See !
my strength , though it be much decay , hath suffice to open this heavy door .
Let u enter and pass up the staircase . ''
Here occur a singular exemplification of the dreamy state of a very old man 's mind .
As they ascend the wide flight of stair the aged clergyman appear to move with caution , occasionally stand aside , and oftener bend his head , a it be in salutation , thus practise all the gesture of one who make his way through a throng .

`` Reverend sir , '' say his attendant , who conceive this a very suitable prelude to their further search , `` would it not be well that the people join with u in prayer ? ''
`` Well-a-day ! ''
cry the old clergyman , star strangely around him .
`` Art thou here with me , and none other ?
Verily , past time be present to me , and I deem that I be to make a funeral prayer , a many a time heretofore , from the head of this staircase .
Of a truth , I saw the shade of many that be go .
Yea , I have pray at their burial , one after another , and the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet hath see them to their graf . ''
Being now more thoroughly awake to their present purpose , he take his staff and struck forcibly on the floor , till there come an echo from each deserted chamber , but no menial to answer their summons .
They therefore walk along the passage , and again paused , opposite to the great front window , through which be see the crowd in the shadow and partial moonlight of the street beneath .
On their right hand be the open door of a chamber , and a closed one on their left .
The clergyman point his cane to the carve oak panel of the latter .
`` Within that chamber , '' observe he , `` a whole lifetime since , do I sit by the death-bed of a goodly young man who , be now at the last gasp -- '' Apparently , there be some powerful excitement in the idea which have now flash across his mind .
He snatch the torch from his companion 's hand , and throw open the door with such sudden violence that the flame be extinguish , leave them no other light than the moonbeam which fell through two window into the spacious chamber .
It be sufficient to discover all that could be know .
In a high-backed oaken arm-chair , upright , with her hand clasped across her breast and her head thrown back , sit the Old Maid in the Winding-Sheet .
The stately dame have fall on her knee with her forehead on the holy knee of the Old Maid , one hand upon the floor and the other press convulsively against her heart .
It clutch a lock of hair -- once sable , now discolor with a greenish mould .
As the priest and layman advance into the chamber the Old Maid 's feature assume such a semblance of shift expression that they trust to hear the whole mystery explain by a single word .
But it be only the shadow of a tattered curtain wave betwixt the dead face and the moonlight .
`` Both dead ! ''
say the venerable man .
`` Then who shall divulge the secret ?
Methinks it glimmer to and fro in my mind like the light and shadow across the Old Maid 's face .
And now 't be go ! ''
PETER GOLDTHWAITE 'S TREASURE .
`` And so , Peter , you wo n't even consider of the business ? ''
say Mr. John Brown , button his surtout over the snug rotundity of his person and draw on his glove .
`` You positively refuse to let me have this crazy old house , and the land under and adjoin , at the price name ? ''
`` Neither at that , nor treble the sum , '' respond the gaunt , grizzle and threadbare Peter Goldthwaite .
`` The fact be , Mr. Brown , you must find another site for your brick block and be content to leave my estate with the present owner .
Next summer I intend to put a splendid new mansion over the cellar of the old house . ''
`` Pho , Peter ! ''
cried Mr. Brown a he open the kitchen door ; `` content yourself with building castle in the air , where house-lots be cheap than on earth , to say nothing of the cost of brick and mortar .
Such foundation be solid enough for your edifice , while this underneath u be just the thing for mine ; and so we may both be suit .
What say you , again ? ''
`` Precisely what I say before , Mr. Brown , '' answer Peter Goldthwaite .
`` And , a for castle in the air , mine may not be as magnificent a that sort of architecture , but perhaps a substantial , Mr. Brown , a the very respectable brick block with dry-goods store , tailor ' shop and banking-rooms on the low floor , and lawyer ' office in the second story , which you be so anxious to substitute . ''
`` And the cost , Peter ?
Eh ? ''
say Mr. Brown a he withdraw in something of a pet .
`` That , I suppose , will be provide for off-hand by draw a check on Bubble Bank ? ''
John Brown and Peter Goldthwaite have be jointly know to the commercial world between twenty and thirty year before under the firm of Goldthwaite & Brown ; which copartnership , however , be speedily dissolve by the natural incongruity of it constituent part .
Since that event , John Brown , with exactly the quality of a thousand other John Browns , and by just such plod method a they use , have prosper wonderfully and become one of the wealthy John Browns on earth .
Peter Goldthwaite , on the contrary , after innumerable scheme which ought to have collect all the coin and paper currency of the country into his coffer , be a needy a gentleman a ever wore a patch upon his elbow .
The contrast between him and his former partner may be briefly mark , for Brown never reckon upon luck , yet always have it , while Peter make luck the main condition of his project , and always miss it .
While the mean hold out his speculation have be magnificent , but be chiefly confine of late year to such small business a adventure in the lottery .
Once he have go on a gold-gathering expedition somewhere to the South , and ingeniously contrive to empty his pocket more thoroughly than ever , while others , doubtless , be fill theirs with native bullion by the handful .
More recently he have expend a legacy of a thousand or two of dollar in purchase Mexican scrip , and thereby become the proprietor of a province ; which , however , so far a Peter could find out , be situate where he might have have an empire for the same money -- in the cloud .
From a search after this valuable real estate Peter return so gaunt and threadbare that on reach New England the scarecrow in the corn-fields beckon to him a he pass by .
`` They do but flutter in the wind , '' quoth Peter Goldthwaite .
No , Peter , they beckon , for the scarecrow know their brother .
At the period of our story his whole visible income would not have pay the tax of the old mansion in which we find him .
It be one of those rusty , moss-grown , many-peaked wooden house which be scatter about the street of our elder town , with a beetle-browed second story projecting over the foundation , a if it frown at the novelty around it .
This old paternal edifice , needy a he be , and though , be centrally situate on the principal street of the town , it would have bring him a handsome sum , the sagacious Peter have his own reason for never part with , either by auction or private sale .
There seem , indeed , to be a fatality that connect him with his birthplace ; for , often a he have stand on the verge of ruin , and stand there even now , he have not yet take the step beyond it which would have compel him to surrender the house to his creditor .
So here he dwell with bad luck till good should come .
Here , then , in his kitchen -- the only room where a spark of fire take off the chill of a November evening -- poor Peter Goldthwaite have just be visit by his rich old partner .
At the close of their interview , Peter , with rather a mortified look , glance downward at his dress , part of which appear as ancient a the day of Goldthwaite & Brown .
His upper garment be a mixed surtout , woefully fade , and patch with new stuff on each elbow ; beneath this he wear a threadbare black coat , some of the silk button of which have be replace with others of a different pattern ; and , lastly , though he lack not a pair of gray pantaloon , they be very shabby one , and have be partially turn brown by the frequent toasting of Peter 's shin before a scanty fire .
Peter 's person be in keep with his goodly apparel .
Gray-headed , hollow-eyed , pale-cheeked and lean-bodied , he be the perfect picture of a man who have feed on windy scheme and empty hope till he could neither live on such unwholesome trash nor stomach more substantial food .
But , withal , this Peter Goldthwaite , crack-brained simpleton a , perhaps , he be , might have cut a very brilliant figure in the world have he employ his imagination in the airy business of poetry instead of make it a demon of mischief in mercantile pursuit .
After all , he be no bad fellow , but as harmless a a child , and a honest and honorable , and as much of the gentleman which Nature mean him for , a an irregular life and depressed circumstance will permit any man to be .
As Peter stand on the uneven brick of his hearth look round at the disconsolate old kitchen his eye begin to kindle with the illumination of an enthusiasm that never long desert him .
He raise his hand , clench it and smite it energetically against the smoky panel over the fireplace .
`` The time be come , '' say he ; `` with such a treasure at command , it be folly to be a poor man any long .
Tomorrow morning I will begin with the garret , nor desist till I have tear the house down . ''
Deep in the chimney-corner , like a witch in a dark cavern , sit a little old woman mend one of the two pair of stocking wherewith Peter Goldthwaite keep his toe from be frost-bitten .
As the foot be rag past all darning , she have cut piece out of a cast-off flannel petticoat to make new sol .
Tabitha Porter be an old maid upward of sixty year of age , fifty-five of which she have sit in that same chimney-corner , such be the length of time since Peter 's grandfather have take her from the almshouse .
She have no friend but Peter , nor Peter any friend but Tabitha ; so long a Peter might have a shelter for his own head , Tabitha would know where to shelter hers , or , be homeless elsewhere , she would take her master by the hand and bring him to her native home , the almshouse .
Should it ever be necessary , she love him well enough to fee him with her last morsel and clothe him with her under-petticoat .
But Tabitha be a queer old woman , and , though never infect with Peter 's flightiness , have become so accustomed to his freak and folly that she view them all a matter of course .
Hearing him threaten to tear the house down , she look quietly up from her work .
`` Best leave the kitchen till the last , Mr. Peter , '' say she .
`` The sooner we have it all down , the good , '' say Peter Goldthwaite .
`` I be tire to death of living in this cold , dark , windy , smoky , creak , groan , dismal old house .
I shall feel like a young man when we get into my splendid brick mansion , a , please Heaven , we shall by this time next autumn .
You shall have a room on the sunny side , old Tabby , finish and furnish a best may suit your own notion . ''
`` I should like it pretty much such a room a this kitchen , '' answer Tabitha .
`` It will never be like home to me till the chimney-corner get a black with smoke a this , and that wo n't be these hundred year .
How much do you mean to lay out on the house , Mr. Peter ? ''
`` What be that to the purpose ? ''
exclaim Peter , loftily .
`` Did not my great-grand-uncle , Peter Goldthwaite , who die seventy year ago , and whose namesake I be , leave treasure enough to build twenty such ? ''
`` I ca n't say but he do , Mr. Peter , '' say Tabitha , thread her needle .
Tabitha well understand that Peter have reference to an immense hoard of the precious metal which be say to exist somewhere in the cellar or wall , or under the floor , or in some concealed closet or other out-of-the-way nook of the old house .
This wealth , accord to tradition , have be accumulate by a former Peter Goldthwaite whose character seem to have bear a remarkable similitude to that of the Peter of our story .
Like him , he be a wild projector , seek to heap up gold by the bushel and the cart-load instead of scrap it together coin by coin .
Like Peter the second , too , his project have almost invariably fail , and , but for the magnificent success of the final one , would have leave him with hardly a coat and pair of breech to his gaunt and grizzle person .
Reports be various a to the nature of his fortunate speculation , one intimating that the ancient Peter have make the gold by alchemy ; another , that he have conjure it out of people 's pocket by the black art ; and a third -- still more unaccountable -- that the devil have give him free access to the old provincial treasury .
It be affirm , however , that some secret impediment have debar him from the enjoyment of his rich , and that he have a motive for conceal them from his heir , or , at any rate , have die without disclose the place of deposit .
The present Peter 's father have faith enough in the story to cause the cellar to be dig over .
Peter himself choose to consider the legend a an indisputable truth , and amid his many trouble have this one consolation -- that , should all other resource fail , he might build up his fortune by tear his house down .
Yet , unless he felt a lurking distrust of the golden tale , it be difficult to account for his permit the paternal roof to stand so long , since he have never yet see the moment when his predecessor 's treasure would not have find plenty of room in his own strong-box .
But now be the crisis .
Should he delay the search a little long , the house would pass from the lineal heir , and with it the vast heap of gold , to remain in it burial-place till the ruin of the aged wall should discover it to stranger of a future generation .
`` Yes , '' cry Peter Goldthwaite , again ; `` to-morrow I will set about it . ''
The deeper he look at the matter , the more certain of success grow Peter .
His spirit be naturally so elastic that even now , in the blasted autumn of his age , he could often compete with the springtime gayety of other people .
Enlivened by his brightening prospect , he begin to caper about the kitchen like a hobgoblin , with the queer antic of his lean limb and gesticulation of his starved feature .
Nay , in the exuberance of his feeling , he seize both of Tabitha 's hand and dance the old lady across the floor till the oddity of her rheumatic motion set him into a roar of laughter , which be echo back from the room and chamber , a if Peter Goldthwaite be laugh in every one .
Finally , he bound upward , almost out of sight , into the smoke that cloud the roof of the kitchen , and , alight safely on the floor again , endeavor to resume his customary gravity .
`` To-morrow , at sunrise , '' he repeat , take his lamp to retire to bed , `` I 'll see whether this treasure be hide in the wall of the garret . ''
`` And , a we 're out of wood , Mr. Peter , '' say Tabitha , puff and pant with her late gymnastics , `` as fast a you tear the house down I 'll make a fire with the piece . ''
Gorgeous that night be the dream of Peter Goldthwaite .
At one time he be turn a ponderous key in an iron door not unlike the door of a sepulchre , but which , be open , disclose a vault heap up with gold coin as plentifully a golden corn in a granary .
There be chase goblet , also , and tureen , salver , dinner-dishes and dish-covers of gold or silver-gilt , besides chain and other jewel , incalculably rich , though tarnish with the damp of the vault ; for , of all the wealth that be irrevocably lose to man , whether bury in the earth or sink in the sea , Peter Goldthwaite have find it in this one treasure-place .
Anon he have return to the old house as poor a ever , and be receive at the door by the gaunt and grizzled figure of a man whom he might have mistake for himself , only that his garment be of a much elder fashion .
But the house , without lose it former aspect , have be change into a palace of the precious metal .
The floor , wall and ceiling be of burnish silver ; the door , the window-frames , the cornice , the balustrade and the step of the staircase , of pure gold ; and silver , with gold bottom , be the chair , and gold , stand on silver leg , the high chest of drawer , and silver the bedstead , with blanket of woven gold and sheet of silver tissue .
The house have evidently be transmute by a single touch , for it retain all the mark that Peter remember , but in gold or silver instead of wood , and the initial of his name -- which when a boy he have cut in the wooden door-post -- remain a deep in the pillar of gold .
A happy man would have be Peter Goldthwaite except for a certain ocular deception which , whenever he glance backward , cause the house to darken from it glitter magnificence into the sordid gloom of yesterday .
Up betimes rise Peter , seize an axe , hammer and saw which he have place by his bedside , and hie him to the garret .
It be but scantily light up a yet by the frosty fragment of a sunbeam which begin to glimmer through the almost opaque bull-eyes of the window .
A moralizer might find abundant theme for his speculative and impracticable wisdom in a garret .
There be the limbo of departed fashion , age trifle of a day and whatever be valuable only to one generation of men , and which pass to the garret when that generation pass to the grave -- not for safekeeping , but to be out of the way .
Peter saw pile of yellow and musty account-books in parchment cover , wherein creditor long dead and bury have write the name of dead and buried debtor in ink now so fade that their moss-grown tombstone be more legible .
He find old moth-eaten garment , all in rag and tatter , or Peter would have put them on .
Here be a naked and rusty sword -- not a sword of service , but a gentleman 's small French rapier -- which have never leave it scabbard till it lose it .
Here be cane of twenty different sort , but no gold-headed one , and shoebuckles of various pattern and material , but not silver nor set with precious stone .
Here be a large box full of shoe with high heel and peak toe .
Here , on a shelf , be a multitude of phial half fill with old apothecary 's stuff which , when the other half have do it business on Peter 's ancestor , have be bring hither from the death-chamber .
Here -- not to give a long inventory of article that will never be put up at auction -- be the fragment of a full-length looking-glass which by the dust and dimness of it surface make the picture of these old thing look old than the reality .
When Peter , not know that there be a mirror there , catch the faint trace of his own figure , he partly imagine that the former Peter Goldthwaite have come back either to assist or impede his search for the hidden wealth .
And at that moment a strange notion glimmer through his brain that he be the identical Peter who have conceal the gold , and ought to know whereabout it lay .
This , however , he have unaccountably forget .
`` Well , Mr. Peter ! ''
cry Tabitha , on the garret stair .
`` Have you tear the house down enough to heat the teakettle ? ''
`` Not yet , old Tabby , '' answer Peter , `` but that 's soon do , a you shall see . ''
With the word in his mouth , he uplift the axe , and lay about him so vigorously that the dust fly , the board crash , and in a twinkle the old woman have an apron full of broken rubbish .
`` We shall get our winter 's wood cheap , '' quoth Tabitha .
The good work be thus commence , Peter beat down all before him , smite and hew at the joint and timber , unclenching spike-nails , rip and tear away board , with a tremendous racket from morning till night .
He take care , however , to leave the outside shell of the house untouched , so that the neighbor might not suspect what be go on .
Never , in any of his vagary , though each have make him happy while it last , have Peter be happy than now .
Perhaps , after all , there be something in Peter Goldthwaite 's turn of mind which bring him an inward recompense for all the external evil that it cause .
If he be poor , ill-clad , even hungry and exposed , a it be , to be utterly annihilate by a precipice of impend ruin , yet only his body remain in these miserable circumstance , while his aspire soul enjoy the sunshine of a bright futurity .
It be his nature to be always young , and the tendency of his mode of life to keep him so .
Gray hair be nothing -- no , nor wrinkle nor infirmity ; he might look old , indeed , and be somewhat disagreeably connect with a gaunt old figure much the worse for wear , but the true , the essential Peter be a young man of high hope just enter on the world .
At the kindling of each new fire his burnt-out youth rise afresh from the old ember and ash .
It rise exult now .
Having live thus long -- not too long , but just to the right age -- a susceptible bachelor with warm and tender dream , he resolve , so soon a the hidden gold should flash to light , to go a-wooing and win the love of the fair maid in town .
What heart could resist him ?
Happy Peter Goldthwaite !
Every evening -- a Peter have long absent himself from his former lounging-places at insurance office , news-rooms , and book-stores , and a the honor of his company be seldom request in private circle -- he and Tabitha use to sit down sociably by the kitchen hearth .
This be always heap plentifully with the rubbish of his day 's labor .
As the foundation of the fire there would be a goodly-sized back-log of red oak , which after be shelter from rain or damp above a century still hiss with the heat and distilled stream of water from each end , a if the tree have be cut down within a week or two .
Next there be large stick , sound , black and heavy , which have lose the principle of decay and be indestructible except by fire , wherein they glow like red-hot bar of iron .
On this solid basis Tabitha would rear a lighter structure , compose of the splinter of door-panels , ornament moulding , and such quick combustible , which catch like straw and throw a brilliant blaze high up the spacious flue , make it sooty side visible almost to the chimney-top .
Meantime , the gloom of the old kitchen would be chase out of the cobwebbed corner and away from the dusky cross-beams overhead , and drive nobody could tell whither , while Peter smile like a gladsome man and Tabitha seem a picture of comfortable age .
All this , of course , be but an emblem of the bright fortune which the destruction of the house would shed upon it occupant .
While the dry pine be flame and crackle like an irregular discharge of fairy-musketry , Peter sit look and listen in a pleasant state of excitement ; but when the brief blaze and uproar be succeed by the dark-red glow , the substantial heat and the deep singing sound which be to last throughout the evening , his humor become talkative .
One night -- the hundredth time -- he tease Tabitha to tell him something new about his great-granduncle .
`` You have be sit in that chimney-corner fifty-five year , old Tabby , and must have hear many a tradition about him , '' say Peter .
`` Did not you tell me that when you first come to the house there be an old woman sit where you sit now who have be housekeeper to the famous Peter Goldthwaite ? ''
`` So there be , Mr. Peter , '' answer Tabitha , `` and she be near about a hundred year old .
She use to say that she and old Peter Goldthwaite have often spend a sociable evening by the kitchen fire -- pretty much a you and I be do now , Mr. Peter . ''
`` The old fellow must have resemble me in more point than one , '' say Peter , complacently , `` or he never would have grow so rich .
But methinks he might have invest the money well than he do .
No interest !
nothing but good security !
and the house to be tear down to come at it !
What make him hide it so snug , Tabby ? ''
`` Because he could not spend it , '' say Tabitha , `` for as often a he go to unlock the chest the Old Scratch come behind and catch his arm .
The money , they say , be pay Peter out of his purse , and he want Peter to give him a deed of this house and land , which Peter swore he would not do . ''
`` Just a I swear to John Brown , my old partner , '' remark Peter .
`` But this be all nonsense , Tabby ; I do n't believe the story . ''
`` Well , it may not be just the truth , '' say Tabitha , `` for some folk say that Peter do make over the house to the Old Scratch , and that 's the reason it have always be so unlucky to them that live in it .
And as soon a Peter have give him the deed the chest flew open , and Peter catch up a handful of the gold .
But , lo and behold !
there be nothing in his fist but a parcel of old rag . ''
`` Hold your tongue , you silly old Tabby ! ''
cry Peter , in great wrath .
`` They be as good golden guinea a ever bore the effigy of the king of England .
It seem a if I could recollect the whole circumstance , and how I , or old Peter , or whoever it be , thrust in my hand , or his hand , and draw it out all of a blaze with gold .
Old rag indeed ! ''
But it be not an old woman 's legend that would discourage Peter Goldthwaite .
All night long he sleep among pleasant dream , and awake at daylight with a joyous throb of the heart which few be fortunate enough to feel beyond their boyhood .
Day after day he labor hard without waste a moment except at meal-times , when Tabitha summon him to the pork and cabbage , or such other sustenance a she have pick up or Providence have send them .
Being a truly pious man , Peter never fail to ask a blessing -- if the food be none of the best , then so much the more earnestly , a it be more needed -- nor to return thanks , if the dinner have be scanty , yet for the good appetite which be good than a sick stomach at a feast .
Then do he hurry back to his toil , and in a moment be lose to sight in a cloud of dust from the old wall , though sufficiently perceptible to the ear by the clatter which he raise in the midst of it .
How enviable be the consciousness of be usefully employ !
Nothing troubled Peter , or nothing but those phantom of the mind which seem like vague recollection , yet have also the aspect of presentiment .
He often pause with his axe uplift in the air , and say to himself , `` Peter Goldthwaite , do you never strike this blow before ? ''
or `` Peter , what need of tear the whole house down ?
Think a little while , and you will remember where the gold be hide . ''
Days and week pass on , however , without any remarkable discovery .
Sometimes , indeed , a lean gray rat peep forth at the lean gray man , wonder what devil have get into the old house , which have always be so peaceable till now .
And occasionally Peter sympathize with the sorrow of a female mouse who have bring five or six pretty , little , soft and delicate young one into the world just in time to see them crush by it ruin .
But a yet no treasure .
By this time , Peter , be as determine a fate and as diligent a time , have make an end with the uppermost region and get down to the second story , where he be busy in one of the front chamber .
It have formerly be the state-bedchamber , and be honor by tradition a the sleeping-apartment of Governor Dudley and many other eminent guest .
The furniture be go .
There be remnant of faded and tattered paper-hangings , but large space of bare wall ornament with charcoal sketch , chiefly of people 's head in profile .
These be specimen of Peter 's youthful genius , it go more to his heart to obliterate them than if they have be picture on a church wall by Michael Angelo .
One sketch , however , and that the best one , affect him differently .
It represent a ragged man partly support himself on a spade and bend his lean body over a hole in the earth , with one hand extend to grasp something that he have find .
But close behind him , with a fiendish laugh on his feature , appear a figure with horn , a tufted tail and a cloven hoof .
`` Avaunt , Satan ! ''
cry Peter .
`` The man shall have his gold . ''
Uplifting his axe , he hit the horned gentleman such a blow on the head a not only demolish him , but the treasure-seeker also , and cause the whole scene to vanish like magic .
Moreover , his axe break quite through the plaster and lath and discover a cavity .
`` Mercy on u , Mr. Peter !
Are you quarrel with the Old Scratch ? ''

It contain nothing but a brass lamp cover with verdigris , and a dusty piece of parchment .
While Peter inspect the latter , Tabitha seize the lamp and begin to rub it with her apron .
`` There be no use in rub it , Tabitha , '' say Peter .
`` It be not Aladdin 's lamp , though I take it to be a token of as much luck .
Look here , Tabby ! ''

But no sooner have she begin to puzzle over it than she burst into a chuckling laugh , hold both her hand against her side .
`` You ca n't make a fool of the old woman , '' cry she .

No ; this be old Peter Goldthwaite 's writing .
These column of pound , shilling and penny be his figure , denote the amount of the treasure , and this , at the bottom , be doubtless a reference to the place of concealment .
But the ink have either fade or peel off , so that it be absolutely illegible .
What a pity ! ''
`` Well , this lamp be as good a new .
That 's some comfort , '' say Tabitha .
`` A lamp ! ''
think Peter .
`` That indicate light on my research . ''
For the present Peter felt more inclined to ponder on this discovery than to resume his labor .
After Tabitha have go down stairs he stand pore over the parchment at one of the front window , which be so obscured with dust that the sun could barely throw an uncertain shadow of the casement across the floor .
Peter force it open and look out upon the great street of the town , while the sun look in at his old house .
The air , though mild , and even warm , thrilled Peter a with a dash of water .
It be the first day of the January thaw .
The snow lay deep upon the housetop , but be rapidly dissolve into million of water-drops , which sparkle downward through the sunshine with the noise of a summer shower beneath the eaves .
Along the street the trodden snow be a hard and solid a a pavement of white marble , and have not yet grow moist in the spring-like temperature .
But when Peter thrust forth his head , he saw that the inhabitant , if not the town , be already thaw out by this warm day , after two or three week of winter weather .
It gladden him -- a gladness with a sigh breathing through it -- to see the stream of lady glide along the slippery sidewalk with their red cheek set off by quilted hood , boa and sable cape like rose amidst a new kind of foliage .
The sleigh bell jingle to and fro continually , sometimes announce the arrival of a sleigh from Vermont laden with the frozen body of porker or sheep , and perhaps a deer or two ; sometimes , of a regular marketman with chicken , geese and turkey , comprise the whole colony of a barn-yard ; and sometimes , of a farmer and his dame who have come to town partly for the ride , partly to go a-shopping and partly for the sale of some egg and butter .
This couple rode in an old-fashioned square sleigh which have serve them twenty winter and stand twenty summer in the sun beside their door .
Now a gentleman and lady skim the snow in an elegant car shape somewhat like a cockle-shell ; now a stage-sleigh with it cloth curtain thrust aside to admit the sun dash rapidly down the street , whirl in and out among the vehicle that obstruct it passage ; now come round a corner the similitude of Noah 's ark on runner , be an immense open sleigh with seat for fifty people and draw by a dozen horse .
This spacious receptacle be populous with merry maid and merry bachelor , merry girl and boy and merry old folk , all alive with fun and grinning to the full width of their mouth .
They keep up a buzz of babble voice and low laughter , and sometimes burst into a deep , joyous shout which the spectator answer with three cheer , while a gang of roguish boy let drive their snow-balls right among the pleasure-party .
The sleigh pass on , and when conceal by a bend of the street be still audible by a distant cry of merriment .
Never have Peter behold a lively scene than be constitute by all these accessory -- the bright sun , the flash water-drops , the gleaming snow , the cheerful multitude , the variety of rapid vehicle and the jingle-jangle of merry bell which make the heart dance to their music .
Nothing dismal be to be see except that peak piece of antiquity Peter Goldthwaite 's house , which might well look sad externally , since such a terrible consumption be prey on it inside .
And Peter 's gaunt figure , half visible in the projecting second story , be worthy of his house .
`` Peter !
How go it , friend Peter ? ''
cry a voice across the street a Peter be draw in his head .
`` Look out here , Peter ! ''
Peter look , and saw his old partner , Mr. John Brown , on the opposite sidewalk , portly and comfortable , with his furred cloak thrown open , disclose a handsome surtout beneath .
His voice have direct the attention of the whole town to Peter Goldthwaite 's window , and to the dusty scarecrow which appear at it .
`` I say , Peter ! ''
cried Mr. Brown , again ; `` what the devil be you about there , that I hear such a racket whenever I pass by ?
You be repair the old house , I suppose , make a new one of it ?
Eh ? ''

`` If I make it new , it will be new inside and out , from the cellar upward . ''
`` Had not you better let me take the job ? ''
say Mr. Brown , significantly .
`` Not yet , '' answer Peter , hastily shut the window ; for ever since he have be in search of the treasure he hat to have people stare at him .
As he draw back , ashamed of his outward poverty , yet proud of the secret wealth within his grasp , a haughty smile shone out on Peter 's visage with precisely the effect of the dim sunbeam in the squalid chamber .
He endeavor to assume such a mien a his ancestor have probably wear when he glory in the building of a strong house for a home to many generation of his posterity .
But the chamber be very dark to his snow-dazzled eye , and very dismal , too , in contrast with the live scene that he have just look upon .
His brief glimpse into the street have give him a forcible impression of the manner in which the world keep itself cheerful and prosperous by social pleasure and an intercourse of business , while he in seclusion be pursue an object that might possibly be a phantasm by a method which most people would call madness .
It be one great advantage of a gregarious mode of life that each person rectify his mind by other mind and square his conduct to that of his neighbor , so a seldom to be lose in eccentricity .
Peter Goldthwaite have expose himself to this influence by merely look out of the window .
For a while he doubt whether there be any hidden chest of gold , and in that case whether it be so exceedingly wise to tear the house down only to be convince of it non-existence .
But this be momentary .
Peter the Destroyer resume the task which Fate have assign him , nor falter again till it be accomplish .
In the course of his search he meet with many thing that be usually find in the ruin of an old house , and also with some that be not .
What seem most to the purpose be a rusty key which have be thrust into a chink of the wall , with a wooden label append to the handle , bear the initial `` P.G. '' Another singular discovery be that of a bottle of wine wall up in an old oven .
A tradition ran in the family that Peter 's grandfather , a jovial officer in the old French war , have set aside many dozen of the precious liquor for the benefit of toper then unborn .
Peter need no cordial to sustain his hope , and therefore keep the wine to gladden his success .
Many half-pence do he pick up that have be lose through the crack of the floor , and some few Spanish coin , and the half of a broken sixpence which have doubtless be a love-token .
There be likewise a silver coronation medal of George III .
But old Peter Goldthwaite 's strong-box flee from one dark corner to another , or otherwise elude the second Peter 's clutch till , should he seek much far , he must burrow into the earth .
We will not follow him in his triumphant progress step by step .
Suffice it that Peter work like a steam-engine and finish in that one winter the job which all the former inhabitant of the house , with time and the element to aid them , have only half do in a century .
Except the kitchen , every room and chamber be now gutted .
The house be nothing but a shell , the apparition of a house , as unreal a the painted edifice of a theatre .
It be like the perfect rind of a great cheese in which a mouse have dwell and nibble till it be a cheese no more .
And Peter be the mouse .
What Peter have tear down , Tabitha have burn up , for she wisely consider that without a house they should need no wood to warm it , and therefore economy be nonsense .
Thus the whole house might be say to have dissolve in smoke and fly up among the cloud through the great black flue of the kitchen chimney .
It be an admirable parallel to the feat of the man who jump down his own throat .
On the night between the last day of winter and the first of spring every chink and cranny have be ransack except within the precinct of the kitchen .
This fat evening be an ugly one .
A snow-storm have set in some hour before , and be still drive and toss about the atmosphere by a real hurricane which fought against the house a if the prince of the air in person be put the final stroke to Peter 's labor .
The framework be so much weaken and the inward prop remove , it would have be no marvel if in some strong wrestle of the blast the rotten wall of the edifice and all the peaked roof have come crash down upon the owner 's head .
He , however , be careless of the peril , but a wild and restless a the night itself , or a the flame that quiver up the chimney at each roar of the tempestuous wind .
`` The wine , Tabitha , '' he cry -- `` my grandfather 's rich old wine !
We will drink it now . ''
Tabitha arose from her smoke-blackened bench in the chimney-corner and place the bottle before Peter , close beside the old brass lamp which have likewise be the prize of his research .
Peter hold it before his eye , and , look through the liquid medium , behold the kitchen illuminate with a golden glory which also envelop Tabitha and gild her silver hair and convert her mean garment into robe of queenly splendor .
It remind him of his golden dream .

`` The money be find ! ''
exclaim Peter , with a sort of fierceness .
`` The chest be within my reach ; I will not sleep till I have turn this key in the rusty lock .
But first of all let u drink . ''

He then fill two little china teacup which Tabitha have bring from the cupboard .

Its rich and delicate perfume waste itself round the kitchen .
`` Drink , Tabitha ! ''

`` Blessings on the honest old fellow who set aside this good liquor for you and me !
And here 's to Peter Goldthwaite 's memory ! ''
`` And good cause have we to remember him , '' quoth Tabitha a she drink .
How many year , and through what change of fortune and various calamity , have that bottle hoard up it effervescent joy , to be quaff at last by two such boon-companions !
A portion of the happiness of a former age have be keep for them , and be now set free in a crowd of rejoice vision to sport amid the storm and desolation of the present time .
Until they have finish the bottle we must turn our eye elsewhere .
It so chance that on this stormy night Mr. John Brown find himself ill at ease in his wire-cushioned arm-chair by the glow grate of anthracite which heat his handsome parlor .
He be naturally a good sort of a man , and kind and pitiful whenever the misfortune of others happen to reach his heart through the padded vest of his own prosperity .
This evening he have think much about his old partner , Peter Goldthwaite , his strange vagary and continual ill-luck , the poverty of his dwelling at Mr. Brown 's last visit , and Peter 's craze and haggard aspect when he have talk with him at the window .
`` Poor fellow ! ''
thought Mr. John Brown .
`` Poor crack-brained Peter Goldthwaite !
For old acquaintance ' sake I ought to have take care that he be comfortable this rough winter . ''
These feeling grow so powerful that , in spite of the inclement weather , he resolve to visit Peter Goldthwaite immediately .
The strength of the impulse be really singular .
Every shriek of the blast seem a summons , or would have seem so have Mr. Brown be accustom to hear the echo of his own fancy in the wind .
Much amaze at such active benevolence , he huddle himself in his cloak , muffle his throat and ear in comforter and handkerchief , and , thus fortify , bid defiance to the tempest .
But the power of the air have rather the best of the battle .
Mr. Brown be just weather the corner by Peter Goldthwaite 's house when the hurricane catch him off his foot , toss him face downward into a snow-bank and proceed to bury his protuberant part beneath fresh drift .
There seem little hope of his reappearance earlier than the next thaw .
At the same moment his hat be snatch away and whirl aloft into some far-distant region whence no tidings have a yet return .
Nevertheless Mr. Brown contrive to burrow a passage through the snow-drift , and with his bare head bent against the storm flounder onward to Peter 's door .
There be such a creaking and groaning and rattling , and such an ominous shaking , throughout the crazy edifice that the loud rap would have be inaudible to those within .
He therefore enter without ceremony , and grope his way to the kitchen .
His intrusion even there be unnoticed .
Peter and Tabitha stand with their back to the door , stoop over a large chest which apparently they have just drag from a cavity or conceal closet on the left side of the chimney .
By the lamp in the old woman 's hand Mr. Brown saw that the chest be bar and clamp with iron , strengthen with iron plate and stud with iron nail , so a to be a fit receptacle in which the wealth of one century might be hoard up for the want of another .
Peter Goldthwaite be insert a key into the lock .
`` Oh , Tabitha , '' cry he , with tremulous rapture , `` how shall I endure the effulgence ?
The gold !
-- the bright , bright gold !
Methinks I can remember my last glance at it just a the iron-plated lid fell down .
And ever since , be seventy year , it have be blaze in secret and gather it splendor against this glorious moment .
It will flash upon u like the noonday sun . ''
`` Then shade your eye , Mr. Peter ! ''
say Tabitha , with somewhat less patience than usual .
`` But , for mercy 's sake , do turn the key ! ''
And with a strong effort of both hand Peter do force the rusty key through the intricacy of the rusty lock .
Mr. Brown , in the mean time , have draw near and thrust his eager visage between those of the other two at the instant that Peter throw up the lid .
No sudden blaze illuminate the kitchen .
`` What 's here ? ''
exclaim Tabitha , adjust her spectacle and hold the lamp over the open chest .
`` Old Peter Goldthwaite 's hoard of old rag ! ''
`` Pretty much so , Tabby , '' say Mr. Brown , lift a handful of the treasure .
Oh what a ghost of dead and buried wealth have Peter Goldthwaite raise to scare himself out of his scanty wit withal !
Here be the semblance of an incalculable sum , enough to purchase the whole town and build every street anew , but which , vast a it be , no sane man would have give a solid sixpence for .
What , then , in sober earnest , be the delusive treasure of the chest ?
Why , here be old provincial bill of credit and treasury note and bill of land-banks , and all other bubble of the sort , from the first issue -- above a century and a half ago -- down nearly to the Revolution .
Bills of a thousand pound be intermix with parchment penny , and worth no more than they .
`` And this , then , be old Peter Goldthwaite 's treasure ! ''
say John Brown .
`` Your namesake , Peter , be something like yourself ; and when the provincial currency have depreciate fifty or seventy-five per cent , he buy it up in expectation of a rise .
I have hear my grandfather say that old Peter give his father a mortgage of this very house and land to raise cash for his silly project .
But the currency keep sink till nobody would take it a a gift , and there be old Peter Goldthwaite , like Peter the second , with thousand in his strong-box and hardly a coat to his back .
He go mad upon the strength of it .
But never mind , Peter ; it be just the sort of capital for building castle in the air . ''
`` The house will be down about our ear , '' cry Tabitha a the wind shake it with increase violence .
`` Let it fall , '' say Peter , fold his arm , a he seat himself upon the chest .
`` No , no , my old friend Peter ! ''
say John Brown .
`` I have house-room for you and Tabby , and a safe vault for the chest of treasure .
To-morrow we will try to come to an agreement about the sale of this old house ; real estate be well up , and I could afford you a pretty handsome price . ''
`` And I , '' observe Peter Goldthwaite , with revive spirit , `` have a plan for lay out the cash to great advantage . ''
`` Why , a to that , '' mutter John Brown to himself , `` we must apply to the next court for a guardian to take care of the solid cash ; and if Peter insist upon speculate , he may do it to his heart 's content with old Peter Goldthwaite 's treasure . ''
CHIPPINGS WITH A CHISEL .
Passing a summer several year since at Edgartown , on the island of Martha 's Vineyard , I become acquaint with a certain carver of tombstone who have travel and voyage thither from the interior of Massachusetts in search of professional employment .
The speculation have turn out so successful that my friend expect to transmute slate and marble into silver and gold to the amount of at least a thousand dollar during the few month of his sojourn at Nantucket and the Vineyard .
The secluded life and the simple and primitive spirit which still characterize the inhabitant of those island , especially of Martha 's Vineyard , insure their dead friends a longer and dear remembrance than the daily novelty and revolve bustle of the world can elsewhere afford to being of the past .
Yet , while every family be anxious to erect a memorial to it departed member , the untainted breath of Ocean bestows such health and length of day upon the people of the isle a would cause a melancholy dearth of business to a resident artist in that line .
His own monument , record his decease by starvation , would probably be an early specimen of his skill .
Gravestones , therefore , have generally be an article of imported merchandise .
In my walk through the burial-ground of Edgartown -- where the dead have lie so long that the soil , once enrich by their decay , have return to it original barrenness -- in that ancient burial-ground I notice much variety of monumental sculpture .
The elder stone , date a century back or more , have border elaborately carve with flower and be adorn with a multiplicity of death 's - head , crossbones , scythe , hour-glasses , and other lugubrious emblem of mortality , with here and there a winged cherub to direct the mourner 's spirit upward .
These production of Gothic taste must have be quite beyond the colonial skill of the day , and be probably carve in London and bring across the ocean to commemorate the defunct worthy of this lonely isle .
The more recent monument be mere slab of slate in the ordinary style , without any superfluous flourish to set off the bald inscription .
But others -- and those far the most impressive both to my taste and feeling -- be roughly hew from the gray rock of the island , evidently by the unskilled hand of survive friend and relative .
On some there be merely the initial of a name ; some be inscribe with misspelt prose or rhyme , in deep letter which the moss and wintry rain of many year have not be able to obliterate .
These , these be graf where love one sleep .
It be an old theme of satire , the falsehood and vanity of monumental eulogy ; but when affection and sorrow grave the letter with their own painful labor , then we may be sure that they copy from the record on their heart .
My acquaintance the sculptor -- he may share that title with Greenough , since the dauber of sign be a painter as well a Raphael -- have find a ready market for all his blank slab of marble and full occupation in letter and ornament them .
He be an elderly man , a descendant of the old Puritan family of Wigglesworth , with a certain simplicity and singleness both of heart and mind which , methinks , be more rarely find among u Yankees than in any other community of people .
In spite of his gray head and wrinkle brow , he be quite like a child in all matter save what have some reference to his own business ; he seem , unless my fancy mislead me , to view mankind in no other relation than a people in want of tombstone , and his literary attainment evidently comprehend very little either of prose of poetry which have not at one time or other be inscribe on slate or marble .
His sole task and office among the immortal pilgrim of the tomb -- the duty for which Providence have send the old man into the world , a it be with a chisel in his hand -- be to label the dead body , l their name should be forget at the resurrection .
Yet he have not fail , within a narrow scope , to gather a few sprig of earthly , and more than earthly , wisdom -- the harvest of many a grave .
And , lugubrious a his call might appear , he be as cheerful an old soul a health and integrity and lack of care could make him , and use to set to work upon one sorrowful inscription or another with that sort of spirit which impel a man to sing at his labor .
On the whole , I find Mr. Wigglesworth an entertaining , and often instructive , if not an interesting , character ; and , partly for the charm of his society , and still more because his work have an invariable attraction for `` man that be bear of woman , '' I be accustom to spend some hour a day at his workshop .
The quaintness of his remark and their not infrequent truth -- a truth condense and point by the limited sphere of his view -- give a raciness to his talk which mere worldliness and general cultivation would at once have destroy .
Sometimes we would discuss the respective merit of the various quality of marble , numerous slab of which be rest against the wall of the shop , or sometimes an hour or two would pass quietly without a word on either side while I watch how neatly his chisel strike out letter after letter of the name of the Nortons , the Mayhews , the Luces , the Daggets , and other immemorial family of the Vineyard .
Often with an artist 's pride the good old sculptor would speak of favorite production of his skill which be scatter throughout the village graveyard of New England .
But my chief and most instructive amusement be to witness his interview with his customer , who hold interminable consultation about the form and fashion of the desired monument , the buried excellence to be commemorate , the anguish to be express , and finally the low price in dollar and cent for which a marble transcript of their feeling might be obtain .
Really , my mind receive many fresh idea which perhaps may remain in it even longer than Mr. Wigglesworth 's hard marble will retain the deep stroke of his chisel .
An elderly lady come to bespeak a monument for her first love , who have be kill by a whale in the Pacific Ocean no less than forty year before .
It be singular that so strong an impression of early feeling should have survive through the change of her subsequent life , in the course of which she have be a wife and a mother , and , so far a I could judge , a comfortable and happy woman .
Reflecting within myself , it appear to me that this lifelong sorrow -- a , in all good faith , she deem it -- be one of the most fortunate circumstance of her history .
It have give an ideality to her mind ; it have keep her purer and less earthy than she would otherwise have be by draw a portion of her sympathy apart from earth .
Amid the throng of enjoyment and the pressure of worldly care and all the warm materialism of this life she have commune with a vision , and have be the good for such intercourse .
Faithful to the husband of her maturity , and love him with a far more real affection than she ever could have felt for this dream of her girlhood , there have still be an imaginative faith to the ocean-buried ; so that an ordinary character have thus be elevate and refine .
Her sigh have be the breath of Heaven to her soul .
The good lady earnestly desire that the propose monument should be ornament with a carved border of marine plant interwined with twisted sea-shells , such a be probably wave over her lover 's skeleton or strewn around it in the far depth of the Pacific .
But , Mr. Wigglesworth 's chisel be inadequate to the task , she be force to content herself with a rise hang it head from a broken stem .
After her departure I remark that the symbol be none of the most apt .
`` And yet , '' say my friend the sculptor , embody in this image the thought that have be pass through my own mind , `` that broken rise have shed it sweet smell through forty year of the good woman 's life . ''
It be seldom that I could find such pleasant food for contemplation a in the above instance .
None of the applicant , I think , affect me more disagreeably than an old man who come , with his fourth wife hang on his arm , to bespeak gravestone for the three former occupant of his marriage-bed .
I watch with some anxiety to see whether his remembrance of either be more affectionate than of the other two , but could discover no symptom of the kind .
The three monument be all to be of the same material and form , and each decorate in bas-relief with two weep willow , one of these sympathetic tree bend over it fellow , which be to be break in the midst and rest upon a sepulchral urn .
This , indeed , be Mr. Wigglesworth 's standing emblem of conjugal bereavement .
I shudder at the gray polygamist who have so utterly lose the holy sense of individuality in wedlock that methought he be fain to reckon upon his finger how many woman who have once sleep by his side be now sleep in their graf .
There be even -- if I wrong him , it be no great matter -- a glance sidelong at his living spouse , a if he be incline to drive a thriftier bargain by bespeak four gravestone in a lot .
I be well pleased with a rough old whaling-captain who give direction for a broad marble slab divide into two compartment , one of which be to contain an epitaph on his deceased wife and the other to be leave vacant till death should engrave his own name there .
As be frequently the case among the whaler of Martha 's Vineyard , so much of this storm-beaten widower 's life have be toss away on distant sea that out of twenty year of matrimony he have spend scarce three , and those at scattered interval , beneath his own roof .
Thus the wife of his youth , though she die in his and her decline age , retain the bridal dewdrop fresh around her memory .
My observation give me the idea , and Mr. Wigglesworth confirm it , that husband be more faithful in set up memorial to their dead wife than widow to their dead husband .
I be not ill-natured enough to fancy that woman less than men feel so sure of their own constancy a to be willing to give a pledge of it in marble .
It be more probably the fact that , while men be able to reflect upon their lose companion a remembrance apart from themselves , woman , on the other hand , be conscious that a portion of their be have go with the departed whithersoever he have go .
Soul cling to soul , the living dust have a sympathy with the dust of the grave ; and by the very strength of that sympathy the wife of the dead shrink the more sensitively from remind the world of it existence .
The link be already strong enough ; it need no visible symbol .
And , though a shadow walk ever by her side and the touch of a chill hand be on her bosom , yet life , and perchance it natural yearning , may still be warm within her and inspire her with new hope of happiness .
Then would she mark out the grave the scent of which would be perceptible on the pillow of the second bridal ?
No , but rather level it green mound with the surround earth , a if , when she dig up again her buried heart , the spot have cease to be a grave .
Yet , in spite of these sentimentality , I be prodigiously amuse by an incident of which I have not the good-fortune to be a witness , but which Mr. Wigglesworth relate with considerable humor .
A gentlewoman of the town , receive news of her husband 's loss at sea , have bespeak a handsome slab of marble , and come daily to watch the progress of my friend 's chisel .
One afternoon , when the good lady and the sculptor be in the very midst of the epitaph -- which the depart spirit might have be greatly comfort to read -- who should walk into the workshop but the deceased himself , in substance as well a spirit !
He have be pick up at sea , and stand in no present need of tombstone or epitaph .
`` And how , '' inquire I , `` do his wife bear the shock of joyful surprise ? ''
`` Why , '' say the old man , deepen the grin of a death 's - head on which his chisel be just then employ , `` I really felt for the poor woman ; it be one of my best piece of marble -- and to be throw away on a living man ! ''
A comely woman with a pretty rosebud of a daughter come to select a gravestone for a twin-daughter , who have die a month before .
I be impress with the different nature of their feeling for the dead .
The mother be calm and woefully resign , fully conscious of her loss , a of a treasure which she have not always possess , and therefore have be aware that it might be take from her ; but the daughter evidently have no real knowledge of what Death 's doings be .
Her thought knew , but not her heart .
It seem to me that by the print and pressure which the dead sister have leave upon the survivor 's spirit her feeling be almost the same a if she still stand side by side and arm in arm with the depart , look at the slab of marble , and once or twice she glance around with a sunny smile , which , a it sister-smile have fade for ever , soon grow confusedly overshadow .
Perchance her consciousness be truer than her reflection ; perchance her dead sister be a close companion than in life .
