The mother and daughter talk a long while with Mr. Wigglesworth about a suitable epitaph , and finally choose an ordinary verse of ill-matched rhyme which have already be inscribe upon innumerable tombstone .
But when we ridicule the triteness of monumental verse , we forget that Sorrow read far deep in them than we can , and find a profound and individual purport in what seem so vague and inexpressive unless interpret by her .
She make the epitaph anew , though the selfsame word may have serve for a thousand graf .
`` And yet , '' say I afterward to Mr. Wigglesworth , `` they might have make a good choice than this .
While you be discuss the subject I be strike by at least a dozen simple and natural expression from the lip of both mother and daughter .
One of these would have form an inscription equally original and appropriate . ''
`` No , no ! ''
reply the sculptor , shake his head ; `` there be a good deal of comfort to be gather from these little old scrap of poetry , and so I always recommend them in preference to any new-fangled one .
And somehow they seem to stretch to suit a great grief and shrink to fit a small one . ''
It be not seldom that ludicrous image be excite by what take place between Mr. Wigglesworth and his customer .
A shrewd gentlewoman who keep a tavern in the town be anxious to obtain two or three gravestone for the deceased member of her family , and to pay for these solemn commodity by take the sculptor to board .
Hereupon a fantasy arose in my mind of good Mr. Wigglesworth sit down to dinner at a broad , flat tombstone carve one of his own plump little marble cherub , gnaw a pair of crossbones and drink out of a hollow death 's - head or perhaps a lachrymatory vase or sepulchral urn , while his hostess 's dead child wait on him at the ghastly banquet .
On communicate this nonsensical picture to the old man he laugh heartily and pronounce my humor to be of the right sort .
`` I have live at such a table all my day , '' say he , `` and eat no small quantity of slate and marble . ''
`` Hard fare , '' rejoin I , smile , `` but you seem to have find it excellent of digestion , too . ''
A man of fifty or thereabouts with a harsh , unpleasant countenance order a stone for the grave of his bitter enemy , with whom he have wag warfare half a lifetime , to their mutual misery and ruin .
The secret of this phenomenon be that hatred have become the sustenance and enjoyment of the poor wretch 's soul ; it have supply the place of all kindly affection ; it have be really a bond of sympathy between himself and the man who share the passion ; and when it object die , the unappeasable foe be the only mourner for the dead .
He express a purpose of be bury side by side with his enemy .
`` I doubt whether their dust will mingle , '' remark the old sculptor to me ; for often there be an earthliness in his conception .
`` Oh yes , '' reply I , who have muse long upon the incident ; `` and when they rise again , these bitter foe may find themselves dear friend .
Methinks what they mistake for hatred be but love under a mask . ''
A gentleman of antiquarian propensity provide a memorial for an Indian of Chabbiquidick -- one of the few of untainted blood remain in that region , and say to be a hereditary chieftain descend from the sachem who welcome Governor Mayhew to the Vineyard .
Mr. Wiggles-worth exert his best skill to carve a broken bow and scatter sheaf of arrow in memory of the hunter and warrior whose race be end here , but he likewise sculpture a cherub , to denote that the poor Indian have share the Christian 's hope of immortality .
`` Why , '' observe I , take a perverse view of the winged boy and the bow and arrow , `` it look more like Cupid 's tomb than an Indian chief 's . ''
`` You talk nonsense , '' say the sculptor , with the offended pride of art .
He then add with his usual good-nature , `` How can Cupid die when there be such pretty maiden in the Vineyard ? ''
`` Very true , '' answer I ; and for the rest of the day I think of other matter than tombstone .
At our next meeting I find him chisel an open book upon a marble headstone , and conclude that it be mean to express the erudition of some black-letter clergyman of the Cotton Mather school .
It turn out , however , to be emblematical of the scriptural knowledge of an old woman who have never read anything but her Bible , and the monument be a tribute to her piety and good work from the orthodox church of which she have be a member .
In strange contrast with this Christian woman 's memorial be that of an infidel whose gravestone , by his own direction , bore an avowal of his belief that the spirit within him would be extinguish like a flame , and that the nothingness whence he spring would receive him again .
Mr. Wigglesworth consult me a to the propriety of enable a dead man 's dust to utter this dreadful creed .
`` If I think , '' say he , `` that a single mortal would read the inscription without a shudder , my chisel should never cut a letter of it .
But when the grave speaks such falsehood , the soul of man will know the truth by it own horror . ''
`` So it will , '' say I , strike by the idea .
`` The poor infidel may strive to preach blasphemy from his grave , but it will be only another method of impress the soul with a consciousness of immortality . ''
There be an old man by the name of Norton , note throughout the island for his great wealth , which he have accumulate by the exercise of strong and shrewd faculty combine with a most penurious disposition .
This wretched miser , conscious that he have not a friend to be mindful of him in his grave , have himself take the needful precaution for posthumous remembrance by bespeak an immense slab of white marble with a long epitaph in raised letter , the whole to be as magnificent a Mr. Wigglesworth 's skill could make it .
There be something very characteristic in this contrivance to have his money 's worth even from his own tombstone , which , indeed , afford him more enjoyment in the few month that he live thereafter than it probably will in a whole century , now that it be lay over his bone .
This incident remind me of a young girl -- a pale , slender , feeble creature most unlike the other rosy and healthful damsel of the Vineyard , amid whose brightness she be fade away .
Day after day do the poor maiden come to the sculptor 's shop and pas from one piece of marble to another , till at last she pencil her name upon a slender slab which , I think , be of a more spotless white than all the rest .
I saw her no more , but soon afterward find Mr. Wigglesworth cut her virgin-name into the stone which she have choose .
`` She be dead , poor girl ! ''
say he , interrupt the tune which he be whistle , `` and she choose a good piece of stuff for her headstone .
Now , which of these slab would you like best to see your own name upon ? ''
`` Why , to tell you the truth , my good Mr. Wigglesworth , '' reply I , after a moment 's pause , for the abruptness of the question have somewhat startle me -- `` to be quite sincere with you , I care little or nothing about a stone for my own grave , and be somewhat inclined to scepticism a to the propriety of erect monument at all over the dust that once be human .
The weight of these heavy marble , though unfelt by the dead corpse or the enfranchised soul , press drearily upon the spirit of the survivor and cause him to connect the idea of death with the dungeon-like imprisonment of the tomb , instead of with the freedom of the sky .
Every gravestone that you ever make be the visible symbol of a mistaken system .
Our thought should soar upward with the butterfly , not linger with the exuvi that confine him .
In truth and reason , neither those whom we call the living , and still less the depart , have anything to do with the grave . ''
`` I never hear anything so heathenish , '' say Mr. Wigglesworth , perplexed and displease at sentiment which controvert all his notion and feeling and imply the utter waste , and bad , of his whole life 's labor .
`` Would you forget your dead friends the moment they be under the sod ? ''
`` They be not under the sod , '' I rejoin ; `` then why should I mark the spot where there be no treasure hide ?
Forget them ?
No ; but , to remember them aright , I would forget what they have cast off .
And to gain the truer conception of death I would forget the grave . ''
But still the good old sculptor murmur , and stumble , a it be , over the gravestone amid which he have walk through life .
Whether he be right or wrong , I have grow the wiser from our companionship and from my observation of nature and character a display by those who come , with their old grief or their new one , to get them record upon his slab of marble .
And yet with my gain of wisdom I have likewise gain perplexity ; for there be a strange doubt in my mind whether the dark shadowing of this life , the sorrow and regret , have not as much real comfort in them -- leave religious influence out of the question -- a what we term life 's joy .
THE SHAKER BRIDAL .
One day , in the sick-chamber of Father Ephraim , who have be forty year the preside elder over the Shaker settlement at Goshen , there be an assemblage of several of the chief men of the sect .
Individuals have come from the rich establishment at Lebanon , from Canterbury , Harvard and Alfred , and from all the other locality where this strange people have fertilize the rugged hill of New England by their systematic industry .
An elder be likewise there who have make a pilgrimage of a thousand mile from a village of the faithful in Kentucky to visit his spiritual kindred the child of the sainted Mother Ann .
He have partake of the homely abundance of their table , have quaff the far-famed Shaker cider , and have join in the sacred dance every step of which be believe to alienate the enthusiast from earth and bear him onward to heavenly purity and bliss .
His brother of the North have now courteously invite him to be present on an occasion when the concurrence of every eminent member of their community be peculiarly desirable .
The venerable Father Ephraim sit in his easy-chair , not only hoary-headed and infirm with age , but wear down by a lingering disease which it be evident would very soon transfer his patriarchal staff to other hand .
At his footstool stand a man and woman , both clad in the Shaker garb .
`` My brother , '' say Father Ephraim to the surround elder , feebly exert himself to utter these few word , `` here be the son and daughter to whom I would commit the trust of which Providence be about to lighten my weary shoulder .
Read their face , I pray you , and say whether the inward movement of the spirit hath guide my choice aright . ''
Accordingly , each elder look at the two candidate with a most scrutinizing gaze .
The man -- whose name be Adam Colburn -- have a face sunburnt with labor in the field , yet intelligent , thoughtful and trace with care enough for a whole lifetime , though he have barely reach middle age .
There be something severe in his aspect and a rigidity throughout his person -- characteristic that cause him generally to be take for a schoolmaster ; which vocation , in fact , he have formerly exercise for several year .
The woman , Martha Pierson , be somewhat above thirty , thin and pale , a a Shaker sister almost invariably be , and not entirely free from that corpse-like appearance which the garb of the sisterhood be so well calculate to impart .
`` This pair be still in the summer of their year , '' observe the elder from Harvard , a shrewd old man .
`` I would like good to see the hoar-frost of autumn on their head .
Methinks , also , they will be expose to peculiar temptation on account of the carnal desire which have heretofore subsist between them . ''
`` Nay , brother , '' say the elder from Canterbury ; `` the hoar-frost and the black frost hath do it work on Brother Adam and Sister Martha , even a we sometimes discern it trace in our cornfield while they be yet green .
And why should we question the wisdom of our venerable Father 's purpose , although this pair in their early youth have love one another a the world 's people love ?
Are there not many brother and sister among u who have live long together in wedlock , yet , adopt our faith , find their heart purify from all but spiritual affection ? ''
Whether or no the early love of Adam and Martha have render it inexpedient that they should now preside together over a Shaker village , it be certainly most singular that such should be the final result of many warm and tender hope .
Children of neighbor family , their affection be old even than their school-days ; it seem an innate principle interfused among all their sentiment and feeling , and not so much a distinct remembrance a connect with their whole volume of remembrance .
But just a they reach a proper age for their union misfortune have fall heavily on both and make it necessary that they should resort to personal labor for a bare subsistence .
Even under these circumstance Martha Pierson would probably have consent to unite her fate with Adam Colburn 's , and , secure of the bliss of mutual love , would patiently have await the less important gift of Fortune .
But Adam , be of a calm and cautious character , be loth to relinquish the advantage which a single man possess for raise himself in the world .
Year after year , therefore , their marriage have be defer .
Adam Colburn have follow many vocation , have travel far and see much of the world and of life .
Martha have earn her bread sometimes a a sempstress , sometimes a help to a farmer 's wife , sometimes a schoolmistress of the village child , sometimes a a nurse or watcher of the sick , thus acquire a varied experience the ultimate use of which she little anticipate .
But nothing have go prosperously with either of the lover ; at no subsequent moment would matrimony have be so prudent a measure a when they have first part , in the opening bloom of life , to seek a good fortune .
Still , they have hold fast their mutual faith .
Martha might have be the wife of a man who sit among the senator of his native State , and Adam could have win the hand , a he have unintentionally win the heart , of a rich and comely widow .
But neither of them desire good-fortune save to share it with the other .
At length that calm despair which occur only in a strong and somewhat stubborn character and yield to no second spring of hope settle down on the spirit of Adam Colburn .
He seek an interview with Martha and propose that they should join the Society of Shakers .
The convert of this sect be oftener driven within it hospitable gate by worldly misfortune than drawn thither by fanaticism , and be receive without inquisition a to their motif .
Martha , faithful still , have place her hand in that of her lover and accompany him to the Shaker village .
Here the natural capacity of each , cultivate and strengthen by the difficulty of their previous life , have soon gain them an important rank in the society , whose member be generally below the ordinary standard of intelligence .
Their faith and feeling have in some degree become assimilate to those of their fellow-worshippers .
Adam Colburn gradually acquire reputation not only in the management of the temporal affair of the society , but a a clear and efficient preacher of their doctrine .
Martha be not less distinguish in the duty proper to her sex .
Finally , when the infirmity of Father Ephraim have admonish him to seek a successor in his patriarchal office , he think of Adam and Martha , and propose to renew in their person the primitive form of Shaker government a establish by Mother Ann .
They be to be the father and mother of the village .
The simple ceremony which would constitute them such be now to be perform .
`` Son Adam and daughter Martha , '' say the venerable Father Ephraim , fix his aged eye piercingly upon them , `` if ye can conscientiously undertake this charge , speak , that the brother may not doubt of your fitness . ''
`` Father , '' reply Adam , speak with the calmness of his character , `` I come to your village a disappointed man , weary of the world , wear out with continual trouble , seek only a security against evil fortune , a I have no hope of good .
Even my wish of worldly success be almost dead within me .
I come hither a a man might come to a tomb willing to lie down in it gloom and coldness for the sake of it peace and quiet .
There be but one earthly affection in my breast , and it have grow calmer since my youth ; so that I be satisfy to bring Martha to be my sister in our new abode .
We be brother and sister , nor would I have it otherwise .
And in this peaceful village I have find all that I hope for -- all that I desire .
I will strive with my best strength for the spiritual and temporal good of our community .
My conscience be not doubtful in this matter .
I be ready to receive the trust . ''
`` Thou hast spoken well , son Adam , '' say the father .
`` God will bless thee in the office which I be about to resign . ''
`` But our sister , '' observe the elder from Harvard .
`` Hath she not likewise a gift to declare her sentiment ? ''
Martha start and move her lip a if she would have make a formal reply to this appeal .
But , have she attempt it , perhaps the old recollection , the long-repressed feeling of childhood , youth and womanhood , might have gush from her heart in word that it would have be profanation to utter there .
`` Adam have speak , '' say she , hurriedly ; `` his sentiment be likewise mine . ''
But while speak these few word Martha grow so pale that she look fitter to be lay in her coffin than to stand in the presence of Father Ephraim and the elder ; she shudder , also , a if there be something awful or horrible in her situation and destiny .
It require , indeed , a more than feminine strength of nerve to sustain the fixed observance of men so exalted and famous throughout the Beet a these be .
They have overcome their natural sympathy with human frailty and affection .
One , when he join the society , have bring with him his wife and child , but never from that hour have speak a fond word to the former or take his best-loved child upon his knee .
Another , whose family refuse to follow him , have be enable -- such be his gift of holy fortitude -- to leave them to the mercy of the world .
The young of the elder , a man of about fifty , have be breed from infancy in a Shaker village , and be say never to have clasp a woman 's hand in his own , and to have no conception of a close tie than the cold fraternal one of the sect .
Old Father Ephraim be the most awful character of all .
In his youth he have be a dissolute libertine , but be convert by Mother Ann herself , and have partake of the wild fanaticism of the early Shakers .
Tradition whisper at the fireside of the village that Mother Ann have be compel to sear his heart of flesh with a red-hot iron before it could be purify from earthly passion .
However that might be , poor Martha have a woman 's heart , and a tender one , and it quail within her a she look round at those strange old men , and from them to the calm feature of Adam Colburn .
But , perceive that the elder eye her doubtfully , she gasp for breath and again speak .
`` With what strength be leave me by my many trouble , '' say she , `` I be ready to undertake this charge , and to do my best in it . ''
`` My child , join your hand , '' say Father Ephraim .
They do so .
The elder stand up around , and the father feebly raise himself to a more erect position , but continue sit in his great chair .
`` I have bid you to join your hand , '' say he , `` not in earthly affection , for ye have cast off it chain for ever , but a brother and sister in spiritual love and helper of one another in your allotted task .
Teach unto others the faith which ye have receive .
Open wide your gate -- I deliver you the key thereof -- open them wide to all who will give up the iniquity of the world and come hither to lead life of purity and peace .
Receive the weary one who have know the vanity of earth ; receive the little child , that they may never learn that miserable lesson .
And a blessing be upon your labor ; so that the time may hasten on when the mission of Mother Ann shall have work it full effect , when child shall no more be bear and die , and the last survivor of mortal race -- some old and weary man like me -- shall see the sun go down nevermore to rise on a world of sin and sorrow . ''
The age father sank back exhaust , and the surround elder deem , with good reason , that the hour be come when the new head of the village must enter on their patriarchal duty .
In their attention to Father Ephraim their eye be turn from Martha Pierson , who grow paler and paler , unnoticed even by Adam Colburn .
He , indeed , have withdraw his hand from hers and fold his arm with a sense of satisfied ambition .
But paler and paler grow Martha by his side , till , like a corpse in it burial-clothes , she sink down at the foot of her early lover ; for , after many trial firmly borne , her heart could endure the weight of it desolate agony no longer .
NIGHT-SKETCHES , BENEATH AN UMBRELLA .
Pleasant be a rainy winter 's day within-doors .
The best study for such a day -- or the best amusement : call it what you will -- be a book of travel describe scene the most unlike that sombre one which be mistily present through the window .
I have experience that Fancy be then most successful in impart distinct shape and vivid color to the object which the author have spread upon his page , and that his word become magic spell to summon up a thousand varied picture .
Strange landscape glimmer through the familiar wall of the room , and outlandish figure thrust themselves almost within the sacred precinct of the hearth .
Small a my chamber be , it have space enough to contain the ocean-like circumference of an Arabian desert , it parched sand track by the long line of a caravan with the camel patiently journey through the heavy sunshine .
Though my ceiling be not lofty , yet I can pile up the mountain of Central Asia beneath it till their summit shine far above the cloud of the middle atmosphere .
And with my humble mean -- a wealth that be not taxable -- I can transport hither the magnificent merchandise of an Oriental bazaar , and call a crowd of purchaser from distant country to pay a fair profit for the precious article which be display on all side .
True it be , however , that amid the bustle of traffic , or whatever else may seem to be go on around me , the raindrop will occasionally be hear to patter against my window-panes , which look forth upon one of the quiet street in a New England town .
After a time , too , the vision vanish , and will not appear again at my bidding .
Then , it be nightfall , a gloomy sense of unreality depresses my spirit , and impels me to venture out before the clock shall strike bedtime to satisfy myself that the world be not entirely make up of such shadowy material a have busy me throughout the day .
A dreamer may dwell so long among fantasy that the thing without him will seem as unreal a those within .
When eve have fairly set in , therefore , I sally forth , tightly button my shaggy overcoat and hoist my umbrella , the silken dome of which immediately resound with the heavy drumming of the invisible raindrop .
Pausing on the low doorstep , I contrast the warmth and cheerfulness of my deserted fireside with the drear obscurity and chill discomfort into which I be about to plunge .
Now come fearful augury innumerable a the drop of rain .
Did not my manhood cry shame upon me , I should turn back within-doors , resume my elbow-chair , my slipper and my book , pas such an evening of sluggish enjoyment a the day have be , and go to bed inglorious .
The same shivering reluctance , no doubt , have quell for a moment the adventurous spirit of many a traveller when his foot , which be destine to measure the earth around , be leave their last track in the home-paths .
In my own case poor human nature may be allow a few misgiving .
I look upward and discern no sky , not even an unfathomable void , but only a black , impenetrable nothingness , a though heaven and all it light be blot from the system of the universe .
It be a if Nature be dead and the world have put on black and the cloud be weep for her .
With their tear upon my cheek I turn my eye earthward , but find little consolation here below .
A lamp be burn dimly at the distant corner , and throw just enough of light along the street to show , and exaggerate by so faintly show , the peril and difficulty which beset my path .
Yonder dingily-white remnant of a huge snowbank , which will yet cumber the sidewalk till the latter day of March , over or through that wintry waste must I stride onward .
Beyond lie a certain Slough of Despond , a concoction of mud and liquid filth , ankle-deep , leg-deep , neck-deep -- in a word , of unknown bottom -- on which the lamplight do not even glimmer , but which I have occasionally watch in the gradual growth of it horror from morn till nightfall .
Should I flounder into it depth , farewell to upper earth !
And hark !
how roughly resound the roaring of a stream the turbulent career of which be partially redden by the gleam of the lamp , but elsewhere brawls noisily through the dense gloom !
Oh , should I be sweep away in ford that impetuous and unclean torrent , the coroner will have a job with an unfortunate gentleman who would fain end his trouble anywhere but in a mud-puddle .
Pshaw !
I will linger not another instant at arm 's - length from these dim terror , which grow more obscurely formidable the longer I delay to grapple with them .
Now for the onset , and , lo !
with little damage save a dash of rain in the face and breast , a splash of mud high up the pantaloon and the left boot full of ice-cold water , behold me at the corner of the street .
The lamp throw down a circle of red light around me , and twinkle onward from corner to corner I discern other beacon , marshal my way to a brighter scene .
But this be a lonesome and dreary spot .
The tall edifice bid gloomy defiance to the storm with their blind all close , even a a man wink when he face a spattering gust .
How loudly tinkle the collected rain down the tin spout !
The puff of wind be boisterous , and seem to assail me from various quarter at once .
I have often observe that this corner be a haunt and loitering-place for those wind which have no work to do upon the deep dashing ship against our iron-bound shore , nor in the forest tear up the sylvan giant with half a rood of soil at their vast root .
Here they amuse themselves with less freak of mischief .
See , at this moment , how they assail yonder poor woman who be pass just within the verge of the lamplight !
One blast struggle for her umbrella and turn it wrong side outward , another whisk the cape of her cloak across her eye , while a third take most unwarrantable liberty with the low part of her attire .
Happily , the good dame be no gossamer , but a figure of rotundity and fleshly substance ; else would these aerial tormentor whirl her aloft like a witch upon a broomstick , and set her down , doubtless , in the filthy kennel hereabout .
From hence I tread upon firm pavement into the centre of the town .
Here there be almost a brilliant an illumination a when some great victory have be win either on the battlefield or at the poll .
Two row of shop with window down nearly to the ground cast a glow from side to side , while the black night hang overhead like a canopy , and thus keep the splendor from diffuse itself away .
The wet sidewalk gleam with a broad sheet of red light .
The raindrop glitter a if the sky be pour down ruby .
The spout gush with fire .
Methinks the scene be an emblem of the deceptive glare which mortal throw around their footstep in the moral world , thus bedazzle themselves till they forget the impenetrable obscurity that hem them in , and that can be dispel only by radiance from above .
And , after all , it be a cheerless scene , and cheerless be the wanderer in it .
Here come one who have so long be familiar with tempestuous weather that he take the bluster of the storm for a friendly greeting , a if it should say , `` How fare ye , brother ? ''
He be a retired sea-captain wrap in some nameless garment of the pea-jacket order , and be now lay his course toward the marine-insurance office , there to spin yarn of gale and shipwreck with a crew of old seadogs like himself .
The blast will put in it word among their hoarse voice , and be understand by all of them .
Next I meet an unhappy slipshod gentleman with a cloak flung hastily over his shoulder , run a race with boisterous wind and strive to glide between the drop of rain .
Some domestic emergency or other have blow this miserable man from his warm fireside in quest of a doctor .
See that little vagabond !
How carelessly he have take his stand right underneath a spout while star at some object of curiosity in a shop-window !
Surely the rain be his native element ; he must have fall with it from the cloud , a frog be suppose to do .
Here be a picture , and a pretty one -- a young man and a girl , both envelop in cloak and huddle beneath the scanty protection of a cotton umbrella .
She wear rubber overshoe , but he be in his dancing-pumps , and they be on their way no doubt , to some cotillon-party or subscription-ball at a dollar a head , refreshment include .
Thus they struggle against the gloomy tempest , lure onward by a vision of festal splendor .
But ah !
a most lamentable disaster !
Bewildered by the red , blue and yellow meteor in an apothecary 's window , they have step upon a slippery remnant of ice , and be precipitate into a confluence of swollen flood at the corner of two street .
Luckless lover !
Were it my nature to be other than a looker-on in life , I would attempt your rescue .
Since that may not be , I vow , should you be drown , to weave such a pathetic story of your fate a shall call forth tear enough to drown you both anew .
Do ye touch bottom , my young friend ?
Yes ; they emerge like a water-nymph and a river-deity , and paddle hand in hand out of the depth of the dark pool .
They hurry homeward , drip , disconsolate , abash , but with love too warm to be chill by the cold water .
They have stand a test which prove too strong for many .
Faithful though over head and ear in trouble !
Onward I go , derive a sympathetic joy or sorrow from the varied aspect of mortal affair even a my figure catch a gleam from the light window or be blacken by an interval of darkness .
Not that mine be altogether a chameleon spirit with no hue of it own .
Now I pass into a more retired street where the dwelling of wealth and poverty be intermingle , present a range of strongly-contrasted picture .
Here , too , may be find the golden mean .
Through yonder casement I discern a family circle -- the grandmother , the parent and the child -- all flickering , shadow-like , in the glow of a wood-fire .
-- Bluster , fierce blast , and beat , thou wintry rain , against the window-panes !
Ye can not damp the enjoyment of that fireside .
-- Surely my fate be hard that I should be wander homeless here , take to my bosom night and storm and solitude instead of wife and child .
Peace , murmurer !
Doubt not that darker guest be sit round the hearth , though the warm blaze hide all but blissful image .
Well , here be still a bright scene -- a stately mansion illuminate for a ball , with cut-glass chandelier and alabaster lamp in every room , and sunny landscape hang round the wall .
See !
a coach have stop , whence emerge a slender beauty who , canopy by two umbrella , glide within the portal and vanishes amid lightsome thrill of music .
Will she ever feel the night-wind and the rain ?
Perhaps -- perhaps !
And will Death and Sorrow ever enter that proud mansion ?
As surely a the dancer will be gay within it hall to-night .
Such thought sadden yet satisfy my heart , for they teach me that the poor man in this mean , weatherbeaten hovel , without a fire to cheer him , may call the rich his brother -- brother by Sorrow , who must be an inmate of both their household ; brother by Death , who will lead them both to other home .
Onward , still onward , I plunge into the night .
Now have I reach the utmost limit of the town , where the last lamp struggle feebly with the darkness like the farthest star that stand sentinel on the border of uncreated space .
It be strange what sensation of sublimity may spring from a very humble source .
Such be suggest by this hollow roar of a subterranean cataract where the mighty stream of a kennel precipitate itself beneath an iron grate and be see no more on earth .
Listen a while to it voice of mystery , and Fancy will magnify it till you start and smile at the illusion .
And now another sound -- the rumbling of wheel a the mail-coach , outward bound , roll heavily off the pavement and splash through the mud and water of the road .
All night long the poor passenger will be toss to and fro between drowsy watch and troubled sleep , and will dream of their own quiet bed and awake to find themselves still jolt onward .
Happier my lot , who will straightway hie me to my familiar room and toast myself comfortably before the fire , muse and fitfully doze and fancy a strangeness in such sight a all may see .
But first let me gaze at this solitary figure who come hitherward with a tin lantern which throw the circular pattern of it punched hole on the ground about him .
He pass fearlessly into the unknown gloom , whither I will not follow him .
This figure shall supply me with a moral wherewith , for lack of a more appropriate one , I may wind up my sketch .
He fear not to tread the dreary path before him , because his lantern , which be kindle at the fireside of his home , will light him back to that same fireside again .
And thus we , night-wanderers through a stormy and dismal world , if we bear the lamp of Faith enkindle at a celestial fire , it will surely lead u home to that heaven whence it radiance be borrow .
ENDICOTT AND THE RED CROSS .
At noon of an autumnal day more than two century ago the English color be display by the standard bearer of the Salem train-band , which have muster for martial exercise under the order of John Endicott .
It be a period when the religious exile be accustom often to buckle on their armor and practise the handling of their weapon of war .
Since the first settlement of New England it prospect have never be so dismal .
The dissension between Charles I. and his subject be then , and for several year afterward , confine to the floor of Parliament .
The measure of the king and ministry be render more tyrannically violent by an opposition which have not yet acquire sufficient confidence in it own strength to resist royal injustice with the sword .
The bigoted and haughty primate Laud , archbishop of Canterbury , control the religious affair of the realm , and be consequently invest with power which might have work the utter ruin of the two Puritan colony , Plymouth and Massachusetts .
There be evidence on record that our forefather perceive their danger , but be resolve that their infant country should not fall without a struggle , even beneath the giant strength of the king 's right arm .
Such be the aspect of the time when the fold of the English banner with the red cross in it field be fling out over a company of Puritans .
Their leader , the famous Endicott , be a man of stern and resolute countenance , the effect of which be heighten by a grizzled beard that sweep the upper portion of his breastplate .
This piece of armor be so highly polished that the whole surround scene have it image in the glittering steel .
The central object in the mirrored picture be an edifice of humble architecture with neither steeple nor bell to proclaim it -- what , nevertheless , it be -- the house of prayer .
A token of the peril of the wilderness be see in the grim head of a wolf which have just be slain within the precinct of the town , and , accord to the regular mode of claim the bounty , be nail on the porch of the meeting-house .
The blood be still plash on the doorstep .
There happen to be visible at the same noontide hour so many other characteristic of the time and manner of the Puritans that we must endeavor to represent them in a sketch , though far less vividly than they be reflect in the polished breastplate of John Endicott .
In close vicinity to the sacred edifice appear that important engine of Puritanic authority the whipping-post , with the soil around it well trodden by the foot of evil-doers who have there be discipline .
At one corner of the meeting-house be the pillory and at the other the stock , and , by a singular good fortune for our sketch , the head of an Episcopalian and suspect Catholic be grotesquely encase in the former machine , while a fellow-criminal who have boisterously quaff a health to the king be confine by the leg in the latter .
Side by side on the meeting-house step stand a male and a female figure .
The man be a tall , lean , haggard personification of fanaticism , bear on his breast this label , `` A WANTON GOSPELLER , '' which betoken that he have dare to give interpretation of Holy Writ unsanctioned by the infallible judgment of the civil and religious ruler .
His aspect show no lack of zeal to maintain his heterodoxy even at the stake .
The woman wear a cleft stick on her tongue , in appropriate retribution for have wag that unruly member against the elder of the church , and her countenance and gesture give much cause to apprehend that the moment the stick should be remove a repetition of the offence would demand new ingenuity in chastise it .
The above-mentioned individual have be sentence to undergo their various mode of ignominy for the space of one hour at noonday .
But among the crowd be several whose punishment would be lifelong -- some whose ear have be crop like those of puppy-dogs , others whose cheek have be brand with the initial of their misdemeanor ; one with his nostril slit and sear , and another with a halter about his neck , which he be forbidden ever to take off or to conceal beneath his garment .
Methinks he must have be grievously tempt to affix the other end of the rope to some convenient beam or bough .
There be likewise a young woman with no mean share of beauty whose doom it be to wear the letter A on the breast of her gown in the eye of all the world and her own child .
And even her own child know what that initial signify .
Sporting with her infamy , the lost and desperate creature have embroider the fatal token in scarlet cloth with golden thread and the nice art of needlework ; so that the capital A might have be think to mean `` Admirable , '' or anything rather than `` Adulteress . ''
Let not the reader argue from any of these evidence of iniquity that the time of the Puritans be more vicious than our own , when a we pass along the very street of this sketch we discern no badge of infamy on man or woman .
It be the policy of our ancestor to search out even the most secret sin and expose them to shame , without fear or favor , in the broad light of the noonday sun .
Were such the custom now , perchance we might find material for a no less piquant sketch than the above .
Except the malefactor whom we have describe and the diseased or infirm person , the whole male population of the town , between sixteen year and sixty be see in the rank of the train-band .
A few stately savage in all the pomp and dignity of the primeval Indian stand gaze at the spectacle .
Their flint-headed arrow be but childish weapon , compare with the matchlock of the Puritans , and would have rattle harmlessly against the steel cap and hammer iron breastplate which enclose each soldier in an individual fortress .
The valiant John Endicott glance with an eye of pride at his sturdy follower , and prepare to renew the martial toil of the day .
`` Come , my stout heart ! ''
quoth he , draw his sword .
`` Let u show these poor heathen that we can handle our weapon like men of might .
Well for them if they put u not to prove it in earnest ! ''
The iron-breasted company straighten their line , and each man draw the heavy butt of his matchlock close to his left foot , thus await the order of the captain .
But a Endicott glance right and leave along the front he discover a personage at some little distance with whom it behove him to hold a parley .
It be an elderly gentleman wear a black cloak and band and a high-crowned hat beneath which be a velvet skull-cap , the whole be the garb of a Puritan minister .
This reverend person bore a staff which seem to have be recently cut in the forest , and his shoe be bemire , a if he have be travel on foot through the swamp of the wilderness .
His aspect be perfectly that of a pilgrim , heighten also by an apostolic dignity .
Just a Endicott perceive him he lay aside his staff and stoop to drink at a bubbling fountain which gush into the sunshine about a score of yard from the corner of the meeting-house .
But ere the good man drank he turn his face heavenward in thankfulness , and then , hold back his gray beard with one hand , he scoop up his simple draught in the hollow of the other .
`` What ho , good Mr. Williams ! ''
shout Endicott .
`` You be welcome back again to our town of peace .
How do our worthy Governor Winthrop ?
And what news from Boston ? ''
`` The governor hath his health , worshipful sir , '' answer Roger Williams , now resume his staff and drawing near .
`` And , for the news , here be a letter which , know I be to travel hitherward to-day , His Excellency commit to my charge .
Belike it contain tidings of much import , for a ship arrive yesterday from England . ''
Mr. Williams , the minister of Salem , and of course know to all the spectator , have now reach the spot where Endicott be stand under the banner of his company , and put the governor 's epistle into his hand .
The broad seal be impressed with Winthrop 's coat-of-arms .
Endicott hastily unclosed the letter and begin to read , while , a his eye pass down the page , a wrathful change come over his manly countenance .
The blood glow through it till it seem to be kindle with an internal heat , nor be it unnatural to suppose that his breastplate would likewise become red hot with the angry fire of the bosom which it cover .
Arriving at the conclusion , he shake the letter fiercely in his hand , so that it rustle as loud a the flag above his head .
`` Black tide these , Mr. Williams , '' say he ; `` blacker never come to New England .
Doubtless you know their purport ? ''
`` Yea , truly , '' reply Roger Williams , `` for the governor consult respect this matter with my brother in the ministry at Boston , and my opinion be likewise ask .
And His Excellency entreats you by me that the news be not suddenly noise abroad , l the people be stir up unto some outbreak , and thereby give the king and the archbishop a handle against u . ''
`` The governor be a wise man -- a wise man , and a meek and moderate , '' say Endicott , set his teeth grimly .
`` Nevertheless , I must do accord to my own best judgment .
There be neither man , woman nor child in New England but have a concern as dear a life in these tidings ; and if John Endicott 's voice be loud enough , man , woman and child shall hear them .
-- Soldiers , wheel into a hollow square .
-- Ho , good people !
Here be news for one and all of you . ''
The soldier close in around their captain , and he and Roger Williams stand together under the banner of the red cross , while the woman and the age men press forward and the mother hold up their child to look Endicott in the face .
A few tap of the drum give signal for silence and attention .
`` Fellow-soldiers , fellow-exiles , '' begin Endicott , speak under strong excitement , yet powerfully restrain it , `` wherefore do ye leave your native country ?
Wherefore , I say , have we leave the green and fertile field , the cottage , or , perchance , the old gray hall , where we be bear and breed , the churchyard where our forefather lie bury ?
Wherefore have we come hither to set up our own tombstone in a wilderness ?
A howling wilderness it be .
The wolf and the bear meet u within halloo of our dwelling .
The savage lieth in wait for u in the dismal shadow of the wood .
The stubborn root of the tree break our ploughshare when we would till the earth .
Our child cry for bread , and we must dig in the sand of the seashore to satisfy them .
Wherefore , I say again , have we seek this country of a rugged soil and wintry sky ?
Was it not for the enjoyment of our civil right ?
Was it not for liberty to worship God accord to our conscience ? ''
`` Call you this liberty of conscience ? ''
interrupt a voice on the step of the meeting-house .
It be the wanton gospeller .
A sad and quiet smile flit across the mild visage of Roger Williams , but Endicott , in the excitement of the moment , shake his sword wrathfully at the culprit -- an ominous gesture from a man like him .
`` What hast thou to do with conscience , thou knave ? ''
cry he .
`` I say liberty to worship God , not license to profane and ridicule him .
Break not in upon my speech , or I will lay thee neck and heel till this time to-morrow .
-- Hearken to me , friend , nor heed that accursed rhapsodist .
As I be say , we have sacrifice all thing , and have come to a land whereof the Old World hath scarcely hear , that we might make a new world unto ourselves and painfully seek a path from hence to heaven .
But what think ye now ?
This son of a Scotch tyrant -- this grandson of a papistical and adulterous Scotch woman whose death prove that a golden crown doth not always save an anointed head from the block -- '' `` Nay , brother , nay , '' interpose Mr. Williams ; `` thy word be not meet for a secret chamber , far less for a public street . ''
`` Hold thy peace , Roger Williams ! ''
answer Endicott , imperiously .
`` My spirit be wise than thine for the business now in hand .
-- I tell ye , fellow-exiles , that Charles of England and Laud , our bitter persecutor , arch-priest of Canterbury , be resolute to pursue u even hither .
They be take counsel , saith this letter , to send over a governor-general in whose breast shall be deposit all the law and equity of the land .
They be mind , also , to establish the idolatrous form of English episcopacy ; so that when Laud shall kiss the pope 's toe a cardinal of Rome he may deliver New England , bound hand and foot , into the power of his master . ''
A deep groan from the auditor -- a sound of wrath as well a fear and sorrow -- respond to this intelligence .
`` Look ye to it , brother , '' resume Endicott , with increase energy .
`` If this king and this arch-prelate have their will , we shall briefly behold a cross on the spire of this tabernacle which we have build , and a high altar within it wall , with wax taper burn round it at noon-day .
We shall hear the sacring-bell and the voice of the Romish priest say the mass .
But think ye , Christian men , that these abomination may be suffer without a sword drawn , without a shot fire , without blood spilt -- yea , on the very stair of the pulpit ?
No !
Be ye strong of hand and stout of heart .
Here we stand on our own soil , which we have buy with our good , which we have win with our sword , which we have clear with our ax , which we have till with the sweat of our brow , which we have sanctify with our prayer to the God that bring u hither !
Who shall enslave u here ?
What have we to do with this mitred prelate -- with this crown king ?
What have we to do with England ? ''
Endicott gaze round at the excited countenance of the people , now full of his own spirit , and then turn suddenly to the standard-bearer , who stand close behind him .
`` Officer , low your banner , '' say he .
The officer obey , and , brandish his sword , Endicott thrust it through the cloth and with his left hand rent the red cross completely out of the banner .
He then wave the tattered ensign above his head .
`` Sacrilegious wretch ! ''
cry the high-churchman in the pillory , unable long to restrain himself ; `` thou hast reject the symbol of our holy religion . ''
`` Treason !
treason ! ''
roar the royalist in the stock .
`` He hath deface the king 's banner ! ''
`` Before God and man I will avouch the deed , '' answer Endicott .
-- `` Beat a flourish , drummer -- shout , soldier and people -- in honor of the ensign of New England .
Neither pope nor tyrant hath part in it now . ''
With a cry of triumph the people give their sanction to one of the bold exploit which our history record .
And for ever honor be the name of Endicott !
We look back through the mist of age , and recognize in the rending of the red cross from New England 's banner the first omen of that deliverance which our father consummate after the bone of the stern Puritan have lie more than a century in the dust .
THE LILY 'S QUEST .
AN APOLOGUE .
Two lover once upon a time have plan a little summer-house in the form of an antique temple which it be their purpose to consecrate to all manner of refined and innocent enjoyment .
There they would hold pleasant intercourse with one another and the circle of their familiar friend ; there they would give festival of delicious fruit ; there they would hear lightsome music intermingle with the strain of pathos which make joy more sweet ; there they would read poetry and fiction and permit their own mind to flit away in day-dreams and romance ; there , in short -- for why should we shape out the vague sunshine of their hope ?
-- there all pure delight be to cluster like rose among the pillar of the edifice and blossom ever new and spontaneously .
So one breezy and cloudless afternoon Adam Forrester and Lilias Fay set out upon a ramble over the wide estate which they be to possess together , seek a proper site for their temple of happiness .
They be themselves a fair and happy spectacle , fit priest and priestess for such a shrine , although , make poetry of the pretty name of Lilias , Adam Forrester be wont to call her `` Lily '' because her form be a fragile and her cheek almost a pale .
As they pass hand in hand down the avenue of droop elm that lead from the portal of Lilias Fay 's paternal mansion they seem to glance like winged creature through the strip of sunshine , and to scatter brightness where the deep shadow fell .
But , set forth at the same time with this youthful pair , there be a dismal figure wrap in a black velvet cloak that might have be make of a coffin-pall , and with a sombre hat such a mourner wear droop it broad brim over his heavy brow .
Glancing behind them , the lover well knew who it be that follow , but wish from their heart that he have be elsewhere , a be a companion so strangely unsuited to their joyous errand .
It be a near relative of Lilias Fay , an old man by the name of Walter Gascoigne , who have long labor under the burden of a melancholy spirit which be sometimes madden into absolute insanity and always have a tinge of it .
What a contrast between the young pilgrim of bliss and their unbidden associate !
They look a if mould of heaven 's sunshine and he of earth 's gloomy shade ; they flit along like Hope and Joy roam hand in hand through life , while his darksome figure stalk behind , a type of all the woeful influence which life could fling upon them .
But the three have not go far when they reach a spot that please the gentle Lily , and she pause .
`` What sweeter place shall we find than this ? ''
say she .
`` Why should we seek farther for the site of our temple ? ''
It be indeed a delightful spot of earth , though undistinguished by any very prominent beauty , be merely a nook in the shelter of a hill , with the prospect of a distant lake in one direction and of a church-spire in another .
There be vista and pathway lead onward and onward into the green woodland and vanish away in the glimmering shade .
The temple , if erect here , would look toward the west ; so that the lover could shape all sort of magnificent dream out of the purple , violet and gold of the sunset sky , and few of their anticipated pleasure be dear than this sport of fantasy .
`` Yes , '' say Adam Forrester ; `` we might seek all day and find no lovely spot .
We will build our temple here . ''
But their sad old companion , who have take his stand on the very site which they propose to cover with a marble floor , shake his head and frown , and the young man and the Lily deem it almost enough to blight the spot and desecrate it for their airy temple that his dismal figure have throw it shadow there .
He point to some scattered stone , the remnant of a former structure , and to flower such a young girl delight to nurse in their garden , but which have now relapse into the wild simplicity of nature .
`` Not here , '' cry old Walter Gascoigne .
`` Here , long ago , other mortal build their temple of happiness ; seek another site for yours . ''
`` What ! ''
exclaim Lilias Fay .
`` Have any ever plan such a temple save ourselves ? ''
`` Poor child ! ''
say her gloomy kinsman .
`` In one shape or other every mortal have dream your dream . ''
Then he tell the lover , how -- not , indeed , an antique temple , but a dwelling -- have once stand there , and that a dark-clad guest have dwell among it inmate , sit for ever at the fireside and poison all their household mirth .
Under this type Adam Forrester and Lilias saw that the old man spake of sorrow .
He tell of nothing that might not be record in the history of almost every household , and yet his hearer felt a if no sunshine ought to fall upon a spot where human grief have leave so deep a stain -- or , at least , that no joyous temple should be build there .
`` This be very sad , '' say the Lily , sigh .
`` Well , there be lovely spot than this , '' say Adam Forrester , soothingly -- `` spot which sorrow have not blight . ''
So they hasten away , and the melancholy Gascoigne follow them , look a if he have gather up all the gloom of the deserted spot and be bear it a a burden of inestimable treasure .
But still they ramble on , and soon find themselves in a rocky dell through the midst of which run a streamlet with ripple and foam and a continual voice of inarticulate joy .
It be a wild retreat wall on either side with gray precipice which would have frown somewhat too sternly have not a profusion of green shrubbery root itself into their crevice and wreathe gladsome foliage around their solemn brow .
But the chief joy of the dell be in the little stream which seem like the presence of a blissful child with nothing earthly to do save to babble merrily and disport itself , and make every living soul it playfellow , and throw the sunny gleam of it spirit upon all .
`` Here , here be the spot ! ''
cry the two lover , with one voice , a they reach a level space on the brink of a small cascade .
`` This glen be make on purpose for our temple . ''
`` And the glad song of the brook will be always in our ear , '' say Lilias Fay .
`` And it long melody shall sing the bliss of our lifetime , '' say Adam Forrester .
`` Ye must build no temple here , '' murmur their dismal companion .
And there again be the old lunatic standing just on the spot where they mean to rear their lightsome dome , and look like the embodied symbol of some great woe that in forgotten day have happen there .
And , ala !
there have be woe , nor that alone .
A young man more than a hundred year before have lure hither a girl that love him , and on this spot have murder her and wash his bloody hand in the stream which sing so merrily , and ever since the victim 's death-shrieks be often hear to echo between the cliff .
`` And see ! ''
cry old Gascoigne ; `` be the stream yet pure from the stain of the murderer 's hand ? ''
`` Methinks it have a tinge of blood , '' faintly answer the Lily ; and , be as slight a the gossamer , she tremble and clung to her lover 's arm , whispering , `` Let u flee from this dreadful vale . ''
`` Come , then , '' say Adam Forrester as cheerily a he could ; `` we shall soon find a happy spot . ''
They set forth again , young pilgrim on that quest which million -- which every child of earth -- have try in turn .
And be the Lily and her lover to be more fortunate than all those million ?
For a long time it seem not so .
The dismal shape of the old lunatic still glide behind them , and for every spot that look lovely in their eye he have some legend of human wrong or suffer so miserably sad that his auditor could never afterward connect the idea of joy with the place where it have happen .
Here a heartbroken woman kneel to her child have be spurn from his foot ; here a desolate old creature have pray to the evil one , and have receive a fiendish malignity of soul in answer to her prayer ; here a new-born infant , sweet blossom of life , have be find dead with the impress of it mother 's finger round it throat ; and here , under a shattered oak , two lover have be stricken by lightning and fell blacken corps in each other 's arm .
The dreary Gascoigne have a gift to know whatever evil and lamentable thing have stain the bosom of Mother Earth ; and when his funereal voice have tell the tale , it appear like a prophecy of future woe as well a a tradition of the past .
And now , by their sad demeanor , you would have fancy that the pilgrim-lovers be seek , not a temple of earthly joy , but a tomb for themselves and their posterity .
`` Where in this world , '' exclaim Adam Forrester , despondingly , `` shall we build our temple of happiness ? ''
`` Where in this world , indeed ? ''
repeat Lilias Fay ; and , be faint and weary -- the more so by the heaviness of her heart -- the Lily droop her head and sit down on the summit of a knoll , repeating , `` Where in this world shall we build our temple ? ''
`` Ah !
have you already ask yourselves that question ? ''
say their companion , his shaded feature grow even gloomier with the smile that dwell on them .
`` Yet there be a place even in this world where ye may build it . ''
While the old man speak Adam Forrester and Lilias have carelessly throw their eye around , and perceive that the spot where they have chance to pause possess a quiet charm which be well enough adapt to their present mood of mind .
It be a small rise of ground with a certain regularity of shape that have perhaps be bestow by art , and a group of tree which almost surround it throw their pensive shadow across and far beyond , although some softened glory of the sunshine find it way there .
The ancestral mansion wherein the lover would dwell together appear on one side , and the ivied church where they be to worship on another .
Happening to cast their eye on the ground , they smile , yet with a sense of wonder , to see that a pale lily be grow at their foot .
`` We will build our temple here , '' say they , simultaneously , and with an indescribable conviction that they have at last find the very spot .
Yet while they utter this exclamation the young man and the Lily turn an apprehensive glance at their dreary associate , deem it hardly possible that some tale of earthly affliction should not make those precinct loathsome , a in every former case .
The old man stand just behind them , so a to form the chief figure in the group , with his sable cloak muffle the low part of his visage and his sombre hat overshadow his brow .
But he give no word of dissent from their purpose , and an inscrutable smile be accept by the lover a a token that here have be no footprint of guilt or sorrow to desecrate the site of their temple of happiness .
In a little time longer , while summer be still in it prime , the fairy-structure of the temple arise on the summit of the knoll amid the solemn shadow of the tree , yet often gladden with bright sunshine .
It be build of white marble , with slender and graceful pillar support a vaulted dome , and beneath the centre of this dome , upon a pedestal , be a slab of dark-veined marble on which book and music might be strew .
But there be a fantasy among the people of the neighborhood that the edifice be plan after an ancient mausoleum and be intend for a tomb , and that the central slab of dark-veined marble be to be inscribe with the name of buried one .
They doubt , too , whether the form of Lilias Fay could appertain to a creature of this earth , be so very delicate and grow every day more fragile , so that she look a if the summer breeze should snatch her up and waft her heavenward .
But still she watch the daily growth of the temple , and so do old Walter Gascoigne , who now make that spot his continual haunt , lean whole hour together on his staff and give a deep attention to the work a though it have be indeed a tomb .
In due time it be finish and a day appoint for a simple rite of dedication .
On the precede evening , after Adam Forrester have take leave of his mistress , he look back toward the portal of her dwelling and felt a strange thrill of fear , for he imagine that a the set sunbeam fade from her figure she be exhale away , and that something of her ethereal substance be withdraw with each lessen gleam of light .
With his farewell glance a shadow have fall over the portal , and Lilias be invisible .
His forebode spirit deem it an omen at the time , and so it prove ; for the sweet earthly form by which the Lily have be manifest to the world be find lifeless the next morning in the temple with her head rest on her arm , which be fold upon the slab of dark-veined marble .
The chill wind of the earth have long since breathe a blight into this beautiful flower ; so that a loving hand have now transplant it to blossom brightly in the garden of Paradise .
But ala for the temple of happiness !
In his unutterable grief Adam Forrester have no purpose more at heart than to convert this temple of many delightful hope into a tomb and bury his dead mistress there .
And , lo !
a wonder !
Digging a grave beneath the temple 's marble floor , the sexton find no virgin earth such a be meet to receive the maiden 's dust , but an ancient sepulchre in which be treasure up the bone of generation that have die long ago .
Among those forgotten ancestor be the Lily to be lay ; and when the funeral procession bring Lilias thither in her coffin , they behold old Walter Gascoigne stand beneath the dome of the temple with his cloak of pall and face of darkest gloom , and wherever that figure might take it stand the spot would seem a sepulchre .
He watch the mourner a they lower the coffin down .
`` And so , '' say he to Adam Forrester , with the strange smile in which his insanity be wont to gleam forth , `` you have find no good foundation for your happiness than on a grave ? ''
But a the shadow of Affliction speak a vision of hope and joy have it birth in Adam 's mind even from the old man 's taunting word , for then he know what be betoken by the parable in which the Lily and himself have act , and the mystery of life and death be open to him .
`` Joy !
joy ! ''
he cry , throw his arm toward heaven .
`` On a grave be the site of our temple , and now our happiness be for eternity . ''
With those word a ray of sunshine break through the dismal sky and glimmer down into the sepulchre , while at the same moment the shape of old Walter Gascoigne stalk drearily away , because his gloom , symbolic of all earthly sorrow , might no longer abide there now that the dark riddle of humanity be read .
FOOTPRINTS ON THE SEASHORE .
It must be a spirit much unlike my own which can keep itself in health and vigor without sometimes steal from the sultry sunshine of the world to plunge into the cool bath of solitude .
At interval , and not infrequent one , the forest and the ocean summon me -- one with the roar of it wave , the other with the murmur of it bough -- forth from the haunt of men .
But I must wander many a mile ere I could stand beneath the shadow of even one primeval tree , much less be lose among the multitude of hoary trunk and hidden from the earth and sky by the mystery of darksome foliage .
Nothing be within my daily reach more like a forest than the acre or two of woodland near some suburban farmhouse .
When , therefore , the yearning for seclusion become a necessity within me , I be draw to the seashore which extend it line of rude rock and seldom-trodden sand for league around our bay .
Setting forth at my last ramble on a September morning , I bind myself with a hermit 's vow to interchange no thought with man or woman , to share no social pleasure , but to derive all that day 's enjoyment from shore and sea and sky , from my soul 's communion with these , and from fantasy and recollection or anticipated reality .
Surely here be enough to fee a human spirit for a single day .
-- Farewell , then , busy world !
Till your even light shall shine along the street -- till they gleam upon my sea-flushed face a I tread homeward -- free me from your tie and let me be a peaceful outlaw .
Highways and cross-paths be hastily traverse , and , clamber down a crag , I find myself at the extremity of a long beach .
How gladly do the spirit leap forth and suddenly enlarge it sense of be to the full extent of the broad blue , sunny deep !
A greeting and a homage to the sea !
I descend over it margin and dip my hand into the wave that meet me , and bathe my brow .
That far-resounding roar be Ocean 's voice of welcome .
His salt breath bring a blessing along with it .
Now let u pace together -- the reader 's fancy arm in arm with mine -- this noble beach , which extend a mile or more from that craggy promontory to yonder rampart of broken rock .
In front , the sea ; in the rear , a precipitous bank the grassy verge of which be break away year after year , and fling down it tuft of verdure upon the barrenness below .
The beach itself be a broad space of sand , brown and sparkling , with hardly any pebble intermix .
Near the water 's edge there be a wet margin which glisten brightly in the sunshine and reflect object like a mirror , and a we tread along the glisten border a dry spot flash around each footstep , but grow moist again a we lift our foot .
In some spot the sand receive a complete impression of the sole , square toe and all ; elsewhere it be of such marble firmness that we must stamp heavily to leave a print even of the iron-shod heel .
Along the whole of this extensive beach gambol the surf-wave .
Now it make a feint of dash onward in a fury , yet die away with a meek murmur and do but kiss the strand ; now , after many such abortive effort , it rear itself up in an unbroken line , heighten a it advance , without a speck of foam on it green crest .
With how fierce a roar it fling itself forward and rush far up the beach !
As I throw my eye along the edge of the surf I remember that I be startle , a Robinson Crusoe might have be , by the sense that human life be within the magic circle of my solitude .
Afar off in the remote distance of the beach , appear like sea-nymphs , or some airy thing such a might tread upon the feathery spray , be a group of girl .
Hardly have I behold them , when they pass into the shadow of the rock and vanished .
To comfort myself -- for truly I would fain have gaze a while longer -- I make acquaintance with a flock of beach-birds .
These little citizen of the sea and air precede me by about a stone 's - throw along the strand , seek , I suppose , for food upon it margin .
Yet , with a philosophy which mankind would do well to imitate , they draw a continual pleasure from their toil for a subsistence .
The sea be each little bird 's great playmate .
They chase it downward a it sweep back , and again run up swiftly before the impending wave , which sometimes overtake them and bore them off their foot .
But they float as lightly a one of their own feather on the breaking crest .
In their airy fluttering they seem to rest on the evanescent spray .
Their image -- long-legged little figure with gray back and snowy bosom -- be see as distinctly a the reality in the mirror of the glistening strand .
As I advance they fly a score or two of yard , and , again alight , recommence their dalliance with the surf-wave ; and thus they bore me company along the beach , the type of pleasant fantasy , till at it extremity they take wing over the ocean and be go .
After form a friendship with these small surf-spirits , it be really worth a sigh to find no memorial of them save their multitudinous little track in the sand .
When we have pace the length of the beach , it be pleasant and not unprofitable to retrace our step and recall the whole mood and occupation of the mind during the former passage .
Our track , be all discernible , will guide u with an observing consciousness through every unconscious wandering of thought and fancy .
Here we follow the surf in it reflux to pick up a shell which the sea seem loth to relinquish .
Here we find a seaweed with an immense brown leaf , and trail it behind u by it long snake-like stalk .
Here we seize a live horseshoe by the tail , and count the many claw of that queer monster .
Here we dig into the sand for pebble , and skip them upon the surface of the water .
Here we wet our foot while examine a jelly-fish which the wave , have just toss it up , now seek to snatch away again .
Here we tread along the brink of a fresh-water brooklet which flow across the beach , become shallow and more shallow , till at last it sink into the sand and perishes in the effort to bear it little tribute to the main .
Here some vagary appear to have bewilder u , for our track go round and round and be confusedly intermingled , a if we have find a labyrinth upon the level beach .
And here amid our idle pastime we sit down upon almost the only stone that break the surface of the sand , and be lose in an unlooked-for and overpower conception of the majesty and awfulness of the great deep .
Thus by track our footprint in the sand we track our own nature in it wayward course , and steal a glance upon it when it never dream of be so observe .
Such glance always make u wise .
This extensive beach affords room for another pleasant pastime .
With your staff you may write verse -- love-verses if they please you best -- and consecrate them with a woman 's name .
Here , too , may be inscribe thought , feeling , desire , warm outgushings from the heart 's secret place , which you would not pour upon the sand without the certainty that almost ere the sky have look upon them the sea will wash them out .
Stir not hence till the record be efface .
Now -LRB- for there be room enough on your canvas -RRB- draw huge face -- huge a that of the Sphynx on Egyptian sand -- and fit them with body of correspond immensity and leg which might stride halfway to yonder island .
Child 's - play become magnificent on so grand a scale .
But , after all , the most fascinating employment be simply to write your name in the sand .
Draw the letter gigantic , so that two stride may barely measure them , and three for the long stroke ; cut deep , that the record may be permanent .
Statesmen and warrior and poet have spend their strength in no good cause than this .
Is it accomplish ?
Return , then , in an hour or two , and seek for this mighty record of a name .
The sea will have sweep over it , even a time roll it efface wave over the name of statesman and warrior and poet .
Hark !
the surf-wave laugh at you .
Passing from the beach , I begin to clamber over the crag , make my difficult way among the ruin of a rampart shatter and break by the assault of a fierce enemy .
The rock rise in every variety of attitude .
Some of them have their foot in the foam and be shag halfway upward with seaweed ; some have be hollow almost into cavern by the unwearied toil of the sea , which can afford to spend century in wear away a rock , or even polish a pebble .
One huge rock ascends in monumental shape , with a face like a giant 's tombstone , on which the vein resemble inscription , but in an unknown tongue .
We will fancy them the forgotten character of an antediluvian race , or else that Nature 's own hand have here record a mystery which , could I read her language , would make mankind the wiser and the happier .
How many a thing have trouble me with that same idea !
Pass on and leave it unexplained .
Here be a narrow avenue which might seem to have be hew through the very heart of an enormous crag , afford passage for the rise sea to thunder back and forth , fill it with tumultuous foam and then leave it floor of black pebble bare and glistening .
In this chasm there be once an intersect vein of soft stone , which the wave have gnaw away piecemeal , while the granite wall remain entire on either side .
How sharply and with what harsh clamor do the sea rake back the pebble a it momentarily withdraw into it own depth !
At interval the floor of the chasm be leave nearly dry , but anon , at the outlet , two or three great wave be see struggle to get in at once ; two hit the wall athwart , while one rush straight through , and all three thunder a if with rage and triumph .
They heap the chasm with a snow-drift of foam and spray .
While watch this scene I can never rid myself of the idea that a monster endow with life and fierce energy be strive to burst his way through the narrow pas .
And what a contrast to look through the stormy chasm and catch a glimpse of the calm bright sea beyond !
Many interesting discovery may be make among these broken cliff .
Once , for example , I find a dead seal which a recent tempest have toss into the nook of the rock , where his shaggy carcase lay roll in a heap of eel-grass a if the sea-monster sought to hide himself from my eye .
Another time a shark seem on the point of leap from the surf to swallow me , nor do I wholly without dread approach near enough to ascertain that the man-eater have already meet his own death from some fisherman in the bay .
In the same ramble I encounter a bird -- a large gray bird -- but whether a loon or a wild goose or the identical albatross of the Ancient Mariner be beyond my ornithology to decide .
It repose so naturally on a bed of dry seaweed , with it head beside it wing , that I almost fancy it alive , and trod softly lest it should suddenly spread it wing skyward .
But the sea-bird would soar among the cloud no more , nor ride upon it native wave ; so I draw near and pull out one of it mottled tail-feathers for a remembrance .
Another day I discover an immense bone wedge into a chasm of the rock ; it be at least ten foot long , curve like a scymitar , bejewel with barnacle and small shellfish and partly cover with a growth of seaweed .
Some leviathan of former age have use this ponderous mass a a jaw-bone .
Curiosities of a minuter order may be observe in a deep reservoir which be replenish with water at every tide , but become a lake among the crag save when the sea be at it height .
At the bottom of this rocky basin grow marine plant , some of which tower high beneath the water and cast a shadow in the sunshine .
Small fish dart to and fro and hide themselves among the seaweed ; there be also a solitary crab who appear to lead the life of a hermit , commune with none of the other denizen of the place , and likewise several five-finger ; for I know no other name than that which child give them .
If your imagination be at all accustom to such freak , you may look down into the depth of this pool and fancy it the mysterious depth of ocean .
But where be the hulk and scattered timber of sunken ship ?
where the treasure that old Ocean hoard ?
where the corrode cannon ?
where the corps and skeleton of seaman who go down in storm and battle ?
On the day of my last ramble -- it be a September day , yet as warm a summer -- what should I behold a I approach the above-described basin but three girl sit on it margin and -- yes , it be veritably so -- lave their snowy foot in the sunny water ?
These , these be the warm reality of those three visionary shape that flit from me on the beach .
Hark their merry voice a they toss up the water with their foot !
They have not see me .
I must shrink behind this rock and steal away again .
In honest truth , vow to solitude a I be , there be something in this encounter that make the heart flutter with a strangely pleasant sensation .
I know these girl to be reality of flesh and blood , yet , glance at them so briefly , they mingle like kindred creature with the ideal being of my mind .
It be pleasant , likewise , to gaze down from some high crag and watch a group of child gather pebble and pearly shell and play with the surf a with old Ocean 's hoary beard .
Nor do it infringe upon my seclusion to see yonder boat at anchor off the shore swing dreamily to and fro and rise and sink with the alternate swell , while the crew -- four gentleman in roundabout jacket -- be busy with their fishing-lines .
But with an inward antipathy and a headlong flight do I eschew the presence of any meditative stroller like myself , know by his pilgrim-staff , his saunter step , his shy demeanor , his observant yet abstract eye .
From such a man a if another self have scar me I scramble hastily over the rock , and take refuge in a nook which many a secret hour have give me a right to call my own .
I would do battle for it even with the churl that should produce the title-deeds .
Have not my musing melt into it rocky wall and sandy floor and make them a portion of myself ?
It be a recess in the line of cliff , wall round by a rough , high precipice which almost encircles and shuts in a little space of sand .
In front the sea appear a between the pillar of a portal ; in the rear the precipice be break and intermix with earth which give nourishment not only to cling and twin shrub , but to tree that grip the rock with their naked root and seem to struggle hard for footing and for soil enough to live upon .
These be fir tree , but oak hang their heavy branch from above , and throw down acorn on the beach , and shed their withering foliage upon the wave .
At this autumnal season the precipice be deck with variegated splendor .
Trailing wreath of scarlet flaunt from the summit downward ; tuft of yellow-flowering shrub and rose-bushes , with their redden leaf and glossy seed-berries , sprout from each crevice ; at every glance I detect some new light or shade of beauty , all contrast with the stern gray rock .
A rill of water trickle down the cliff and fill a little cistern near the base .
I drain it at a draught , and find it fresh and pure .
This recess shall be my dining-hall .
And what the feast ?
A few biscuit make savory by soak them in sea-water , a tuft of samphire gather from the beach , and an apple for the dessert .
By this time the little rill have fill it reservoir again , and a I quaff it I thank God more heartily than for a civic banquet that he give me the healthful appetite to make a feast of bread and water .
Dinner be over , I throw myself at length upon the sand and , bask in the sunshine , let my mind disport itself at will .
The wall of this my hermitage have no tongue to tell my folly , though I sometimes fancy that they have ear to hear them and a soul to sympathize .
There be a magic in this spot .
Dreams haunt it precinct and flit around me in broad sunlight , nor require that sleep shall blindfold me to real object ere these be visible .
Here can I frame a story of two lover , and make their shadow live before me and be mirror in the tranquil water a they tread along the sand , leave no footprint .
Here , should I will it , I can summon up a single shade and be myself her lover .
